to which it is attached; for freestanding signs, the applicant shall supply a
plot plan showing the location of the sign on the property, and of all other
signs and structures already existing on the property. The applicant shall also
list the materials of which the sign is to be constructed and, when applicable,
a description of how the sign is to be lighted. (Ord. 344, 7-10-2007)
      6.   All work performed under a permit shall conform to the approved
application and plans and any approved amendment thereof.
      7.   The location of all new construction as shown on the approved plot
diagram or an approved amendment thereof shall be strictly adhered to.
      8.   It shall be unlawful to reduce or diminish the area of a lot or plot
of which a plot diagram has been filed and approved; provided, this shall not
apply when the lot is reduced by reason of a street opening or widening or
other public improvement.
      9.   The permits (village and state) shall be posted on the premises in a
manner easily seen from the street until the completion of the work.
      10.   A certified copy of the approved plans shall be kept on the
premises at all times until the work is completed. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
   F.   Supplemental Permit: A supplemental permit is required if a project is
changed from the original permit in such a way as to increase height, decrease
a setback, or increase the dimension of a sign. A supplemental permit shall be
processed in the same manner as the original permit. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
   G.   Prior Issued Permit: Nothing in this section shall require changes in
the plans, construction or designated use of a building for which a lawful
permit was issued prior to October 29, 1997 (effective date of ordinance 277),
or which has been otherwise lawfully authorized, and the construction of which
shall have been actually begun within ninety (90) days after the provisions of
the zoning regulations become effective.
   H.   Signature Of Authorized Official: Every permit issued by the village
under the provisions of the zoning regulations shall have the signature of the
village clerk/treasurer or other authorized representative affixed thereto.
   I.   Transferability: Permits are not transferable.
   J.   Revocation: The village may revoke a permit or approval issued under
the provisions of these regulations if there has been any false statement or
misrepresentation as to a material fact in the application or plans on which
the permit or approval was based. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
   K.   Special Use Permits: In extraordinary circumstances a special use
permit temporarily permitting a prohibited use may be granted by the board of
trustees. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
   L.   Application, Documentation And Fees:
      1.   Applicant shall submit the completed application and all supporting
documentation (site plans, building plans, sketches, drawings, etc.) to the
village office at least twenty four (24) hours prior to a regular or special
planning and zoning commission meeting and pay the specified fee.
      2.   Applicant or applicant's authorized representative shall attend the
planning and zoning commission meeting at which his application appears on the
agenda. (Ord. 300, 4-10-2001)
   M.   Permit Approval: For buildings, fences, accessory buildings, signs, and
demolition permits that conform to all ordinances and codes, the Village Clerk-
Treasurer or his designee shall issue the appropriate permit within three (3)
working days of receiving the completed application and fee, except that the
Clerk- Treasurer or his designee shall delay issuing the Village permit until a
copy of the State permit, if one is required, is submitted. Permits approved by
the Clerk-Treasurer or his designee shall be summarized and included in the
minutes of the next meeting of the Planning and Zoning Commission. (Ord. 322,
10-14-2003)
   N.   Appeals, Variances And Zone Changes:
      1.   An applicant for a permit that is not recommended for approval by
the Village Clerk-Treasurer or designee may modify the application, appeal to
the Planning and Zoning Commission, or request a variance or a zone change.
      2.   If applicant or applicant's authorized representative fails to
attend any Planning and Zoning Commission meeting or Board of Trustees meeting
at which his application appears on the agenda, the commission or Board of
Trustees may choose not to take action on the application.
      3.   For those applications appealed to the Planning and Zoning
Commission, and found to conform to all ordinances and codes, the Planning and
Zoning Commission shall authorize the Village Clerk- Treasurer or designee to
issue the appropriate permit, subject to receipt of State permit, if required.
      4.   Those applications appealed to the Planning and Zoning Commission
and not conforming to all ordinances and codes, shall be disapproved by the
Planning and Zoning Commission; the applicant may then pursue a variance or a
rezone, or modify the plans to bring them into compliance and resubmit the
permit application.
      5.   The Village Clerk-Treasurer or designee shall inform the applicant
of the appropriate procedures and collect applicable fees and expenses.
      6.   If a variance is requested, the Planning and Zoning Commission shall
set a date and conduct a public hearing within the time prescribed by law to
adopt findings of fact and conclusions of law for consideration by the Board of
Trustees at its next scheduled meeting. Where, by reason of exceptional
narrowness, shallowness or shape of a specific piece of property at the time of
the original adoption of the regulations or exceptional topographical
conditions or other extraordinary or exceptional situation or condition of a
specific piece of property where the strict application of this title would
result in peculiar and exceptional practical difficulties or exception and
undue hardship upon the owner of the property, the commission may make such
recommendations as may be appropriate following such hearing to the Board of
Trustees by proposed findings of fact and conclusions of law; provided,
however, that the owners of all lots within one hundred feet (100'), excluding
public rights-of- way shall be notified by certified mail, return receipt
requested, of any requests for variance and of the hearing on a request at
least fifteen (15) days prior to the hearing on the request for variance by the
commission. Such notice shall include information that the hearing shall
include the commission acting in its capacity as to recommendations to the
Board of Trustees making the final determination and that evidence may be
submitted at either stage. For purposes of notification under this section,
State Statutes shall be followed. The Board of Trustees may then act upon such
recommendations in any manner in which the Board of Trustees may deem
appropriate and lawful. Any person or entity making a formal appearance at the
public hearing before the commission shall be informed at that Public Hearing
that the recommendations of the commission in the matter shall be considered at
the next regular meeting of the Board of Trustees and that the Board of
Trustees may consider additional evidence as a part of its deliberations.
      7.   If a rezone is requested, the Board of Trustees shall set a date and
conduct a public hearing on the request within the time prescribed by law. If
approved and not appealed, the new zone designation becomes effective thirty
(30) days after the decision is filed with the Village Clerk-Treasurer.
      8.   Public hearings, held by the commission or Board of Trustees, shall
be conducted in accordance with applicable State law and procedures as
recommended by the New Mexico Municipal League ensuring compliance with
Battershell v. City of Albuquerque, 108 NM 658 (Ct. App. 1989) and an audio
record of the hearing shall be made. The commission and Board of Trustees shall
allow all amendments to any application which may be necessary in furtherance
of justice. Findings of fact and conclusions of law reflecting the final
decision of the Board of Trustees shall be filed with the Village Clerk-
Treasurer within thirty five (35) days of the conclusion of the hearing before
the Board of Trustees. Such findings shall be signed by all members of the
Board of Trustees in attendance at the hearing, or by the Mayor if so
authorized by all Trustees in attendance; dissenting Trustees must file a
written dissenting opinion. Aggrieved parties have thirty (30) days from the
filing to file a notice of appeal pursuant to State law, and mail a copy of the
notice of appeal to each interested party who appeared at or participated in
the hearing. Notice shall be given by U.S. mail, certified return receipt
requested. The costs of said notification shall be borne by the appellant.
      9.   If a Planning and Zoning Commission hearing, not involving a
variance, results in an appeal or, if a Planning and Zoning Commission finding,
not involving a variance, is appealed, The Village Board of Trustees shall set
a date for a public hearing on the appeal within the time prescribed by law.
Such appeal shall be de novo before the Board of Trustees conducted as set
forth above provided that evidence taken in a hearing before the Planning and
Zoning Commission may be considered as original evidence subject to a legal
objection, the same as if the evidence was originally offered in the hearing
before the Board of Trustees. The Board of Trustees shall allow all amendments
which may be necessary in furtherance of justice. Public hearings require a
minimum of fifteen (15) days notice.
      10.   If no appeal is filed pursuant to State law within the time
proscribed therein from the time the finding is filed with the Village Clerk-
Treasurer, the Village Clerk-Treasurer or his designee shall issue the
appropriate permit if an application has been filed and approved. (Ord. 378, 1-
9-2018)
   O.   Meeting Minutes: Minutes of each Planning and Zoning Commission
meeting, including results of any public hearings, shall be submitted to the
Board of Trustees at the next regular Village Council meeting. (Ord. 322, 10-
14-2003)
9-2-4: FEES:
   A.   Rezoning: A fee as set by the Board of Trustees plus required postage
for notification and publication costs shall be charged for filing application
for rezoning.
   B.   Variance: A fee as set by the Board of Trustees plus required postage
for notification and publication costs shall be charged for filing a request
for variance.
   C.   Building Site Permit: A fee of ten percent (10%) of the State building
permit fee, with a minimum fee set by the Board of Trustees, shall be charged
for a building site permit. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
   D.   Sign And Fence Permit: A fee as set by the Board of Trustees shall be
charged for sign and fence permits. (Ord. 277A, 8-10-1999)
   E.   Supplemental Permit: The fee for a supplemental permit shall be half of
that of the original permit. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
9-2-5: AMENDMENTS AND CHANGES:
The Village Board of Trustees may, from time to time, on its own motion or on
petition, after public notice and hearing at which all parties in interest and
citizens shall have an opportunity to be heard, amend the regulations and zones
herein established. Notice of the proposed amendment shall be given at least
fifteen (15) days in advance of the time and place of the hearing, and shall be
published in the same manner within the limits of the Village as set forth by
statute for publication of ordinances. Such other notice as may be required by
State law shall also be given. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-2-6: BOARD OF APPEALS:
   A.   Established: The Board of Trustees is hereby constituted as a Board of
Appeals to hear any appeal made by a person aggrieved by a recommendation of
the Planning and Zoning Commission.
   B.   Powers: The Board of Appeals shall have the following powers:
      1.   To hear and decide appeals where it is alleged there is an error in
any determination made in the enforcement of the zoning regulations.
      2.   Where, by reason of exceptional narrowness, shallowness or shape of
a specific piece of property at the time of the original adoption of the
regulations or exceptional topographical conditions or other extraordinary or
exceptional situation or condition of a specific piece of property, where the
strict application of this title would result in peculiar and exceptional
practical difficulties or exceptional and undue hardship upon the owner of the
property, the Board of Trustees is hereby empowered to authorize a variation
from strict application to relieve the difficulties or hardships; provided,
however, that the owners of all lots within one hundred feet (100'), excluding
public rights-of-way, shall be notified by certified mail, return receipt
requested, of any requests for variance and of the hearing on a request at
least fifteen (15) days prior to the hearing on the request for variance by the
commission as set forth in this title. For purposes of notification under this
section, State Statutes shall be followed. (Ord. 378, 1-9-2018)
9-2-7: PENALTY; ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Penalty: Any person or corporation who shall violate any of the
provisions of this title or fail to comply therewith or with any of the
requirements thereof, or who shall build or alter any buildings in violation of
any detailed statement or plan submitted and approved hereunder, shall be
guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be liable to a fine of not more than five
hundred dollars ($500.00) and/or imprisonment for up to ninety (90) days. Each
day such violation shall be permitted to exist shall constitute a separate
offense. The owner of any building or premises or part thereof where anything
in violation of this title shall be placed or shall exist, and any architect,
building contractor, agent, person, or corporation employee in connection
therewith and who may have assisted in the commission of any such violation
shall be guilty of a separate offense and upon conviction thereof shall be
fined and/or imprisoned as hereinabove provided.
   B.   Enforcement Procedure: Any possible violation shall be reported to the
Village office. A representative of the Village shall determine if a violation
exists. The owner/contractor of the project shall be notified by certified
letter of the nature of the violation and what procedures shall be taken to
correct same. If no response is received within ten (10) days or if immediate
action is necessary, it shall be the responsibility of the Mayor or his
representative to enforce the ordinance. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
CHAPTER 3
ZONES
SECTION:
9-3-1: Established
9-3-2: Vacated Land
9-3-3: Double Frontage And Odd Shaped Lots
9-3-4: Recently Annexed Territory
9-3-5: Zoning History By Lot And Description
9-3-1: ESTABLISHED:
Zoning regulations as herein set forth are approved and established. The
village is hereby divided into zones, which zones were previously known by the
titles in parentheses below, except such zones as did not heretofore exist, and
shall now be known by the designations set opposite the previous titles as
follows:
   A.   Residential zones:
      R-1 (A) residential housing.
      R-2 (A-M) residential apartments, multiple dwellings.
      R-3 (A-T) residential mobile homes, permanently placed.
   B.   Commercial zones:
      C-1 (D) offices, banks, hospitals, clinics.
      C-2 (D) wholesale and retail.
      C-3 (D) automotive and trailer sales.
      C-4 (D) light manufacturing.
      C-5 car wash.
      C-6 automotive repair.
      C-7 vehicle fueling stations.
      C-8 facilities serving food and/or beverages.
      C-9 auto wrecking yards, kennels.
      C-10 recreation and amusement facilities.
   C.   Recreation and transit accommodation facilities zones:
      T-1 (T-1) (D) tourist lodging and eating facilities.
      T-2 (T-2) (E) recreational vehicle parks.
      T-3 (T-3) (D) stables.
      M-1 mobile home parks.
   D.   Greenbelt:
      G-1 open space, no structures.
      G-2 parks and recreation and related structures.
All of such are adopted by action of the board of trustees and filed in the
village clerk/treasurer's office. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997; amd. Ord. 333, 5-10-
2005; per correspondence dated 5-12-2009)
9-3-2: VACATED LAND:
Whenever any street, alley or any other public way is vacated by official
action of the village, the zones adjoining each side of the street, alley or
public way shall be automatically extended to the center of the vacated area,
and any area included in the vacation shall then and thenceforth be subject to
all appropriate regulations of the extended zones. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-3-3: DOUBLE FRONTAGE AND ODD SHAPED LOTS:
Where any lot abuts two (2) streets which either do not intersect or which
intersect at an angle of less than seventy degrees (70°) with reference to the
lot:
   A.   Permanent unobstructed open space equal to the zone front yard shall be
provided along any side of the lot which abuts a street.
   B.   Setbacks for all odd-shaped lots will be determined by the planning and
zoning commission in accordance with the most applicable rule. (Ord. 277, 10-
29-1997)
9-3-4: RECENTLY ANNEXED TERRITORY:
All territory which may hereafter be annexed to the village shall be subject to
all of the regulations of zone G-1 (open space, no structures), unless the
village board of trustees accepts a zoning plan with the annexation. (Ord. 277,
10-29-1997)
9-3-5: ZONING HISTORY BY LOT AND DESCRIPTION:
The boundaries of the zoning districts as described in section
 9-3-1 of this chapter shall be as set forth in the attachment hereto entitled
"Cloudcroft Zoning History By Lots", which attachment and all information
thereon are made a part of this title and have the force and effect as if the
attachment were fully set forth herein. The attachment, as it may be amended
from time to time to reflect zoning changes, shall be on file with the village
clerk/treasurer. Any property lying within the boundaries of the village which
is not specifically described in the attachment shall be presumed to be zoned
R-1. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
CHAPTER 4
RESIDENTIAL ZONES USE REGULATIONS
ARTICLE A. R-1 ZONE
SECTION:
9-4A-1: Uses Permitted
9-4A-2: Structure Per Lot
9-4A-3: Area
9-4A-4: Setback, Height Restrictions
9-4A-1: USES PERMITTED:
A building or premises shall be used only for the following purposes:
Accessory buildings as provided in section
9-8-2 of this title.
Fences as provided in section
9-8-1 of this title.
Golf course.
Home occupations.
Nonprofit religious, educational and philanthropic institutions, with
exceptions of penal or mental institutions.
Off street parking as provided in chapter 9 of this title.
Preservation of historical sites as provided in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Public park, playground, community building, library.
Retaining walls in accordance with the UBC (uniform building code).
School, church.
Signs as provided in chapter 10 of this title.
Single-family dwellings excluding mobile homes.
Nightly Rentals in single family dwellings provided the owner or vendor has
obtained a Lodger’s Tax License as provided in Section
3-4-6 of the Cloudcroft Village Code. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997; amd. Ord. 385, 1-
14-2020)
9-4A-2: STRUCTURE PER LOT:
There shall be only one main structure per lot provided that multiple adjacent
and contiguous lots owned by the same person or entity may be treated as one
lot provided further that setbacks are observed as set forth herein for
multiple adjacent and contiguous lots owned by the same person or entity. (Ord.
336, 8-9-2005)
9-4A-3: AREA:
Every lot shall have an area of not less than four thousand (4,000) square
feet, unless a lot having a lesser area than herein required was a lot of
record prior to May 5, 1966 (the effective date of ordinance 37). (Ord. 277,
10-29-1997)
9-4A-4: SETBACK, HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
Setback requirements as specified below are the minimum measurement from the
lot line to the physical building and any projections thereof, including any
roof overhang that exceeds three feet (3'). Landings forty four inches (44")
long having a width not more than the width of the door served with stairs that
same width shall not be considered a projection.
   A.   Front Yard: A minimum front yard setback of twenty five feet (25') or
twenty five percent (25%) of the depth of the lot, whichever is smaller.
   B.   Side Yard: A minimum side yard setback of seven and one-half feet (7 1/
2') along each side lot line. Lots fifty feet (50') or less in width may have a
side yard setback of five feet (5'). The side yard on the street side of a
corner lot shall be not less than fifteen feet (15') in width.
   C.   Rear Yard: A minimum rear yard setback of thirty feet (30') or twenty
percent (20%) of the depth of the entire lot, whichever amount is smaller.
   D.   Height: No part of any building or structure shall exceed thirty five
feet (35') in height above grade. (See definition for "grade" set forth in
section
9-1-3 of this title.) (Ord. 344, 7-10-2007)
ARTICLE B. R-2 ZONE
SECTION:
9-4B-1: Uses Permitted
9-4B-2: Area
9-4B-3: Density
9-4B-4: Setback, Height Restrictions
9-4B-5: Refuse Area
9-4B-1: USES PERMITTED:
A building or premises shall be used only for the following purposes:
Accessory buildings as provided in Section
9-8-2 of this Title.
Any use allowed in Zone R-1.
Boarding houses.
Fences as provided in Section
9-8-1 of this Title.
Multiple dwellings, condominiums, apartments, multi-plexes.
Off-street parking as provided in
Chapter 9 of this Title.
Preservation of historical sites as provided in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Retaining walls in accordance with the UBC (Uniform Building Code).
Row dwellings, townhouses.
Signs as provided in
Chapter 10 of this Title. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-4B-2: AREA:
There shall be at least one thousand five hundred (1,500) square feet of land
area for each dwelling unit. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-4B-3: DENSITY:
If any project or complex intended for development under a common plan exceeds
forty five thousand (45,000) square feet of land area, exclusive of public
streets and rights of way, the maximum allowable number of dwelling units shall
be one per two thousand two hundred fifty (2,250) square feet of land area.
(Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-4B-4: SETBACK, HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
Setback requirements as specified below are to be considered the minimum
measurement from the lot line to the physical building and any projections
thereof, including any roof overhang that exceeds three feet (3'). Landings
forty four inches (44") long having a width not more than the width of the door
served with stairs that same width shall not be considered a projection.
   A.   Front Yard: A minimum front yard setback of fifteen feet (15') for
standard buildings and for complexes where common open space or courtyards are
not provided. For projects or complexes in which not more than sixty percent
(60%) of the total land area is used for buildings, an eight foot (8') front
setback will be allowed. Under the sixty percent (60%) option, the open space
shall at no time be diminished.
   B.   Side Yard:
      1.   A minimum side yard setback of seven and one-half feet (71/2') along
each side lot line.
      2.   On any corner lot, the least width of any side yard along a side
street lot line shall be eight feet (8').
      3.   For projects or complexes in which not more than sixty percent (60%)
of the total land area is used for buildings, a zero side line or common wall
will be allowed; providing, however, that the side yard restrictions shall
apply to the extreme (end) units in respect to the adjacent street or lot line
of ownership other than the proposed project or complex.
   C.   Rear Yard: A minimum ten foot (10') rear yard setback on every lot.
   D.   Height: No part of any building or structure shall exceed thirty feet
(30') in height above grade. (See definition for "grade" as set forth in
Section
 9-1-3 of this Title.) (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-4B-5: REFUSE AREA:
An area for refuse containers shall be provided on the property. (Ord. 277, 10-
29-1997)
ARTICLE C. R-3 ZONE
SECTION:
9-4C-1: Uses Permitted
9-4C-2: Structure Per Lot
9-4C-1: USES PERMITTED:
A building or premises shall be used only for the following purposes:
Accessory buildings as provided in section
9-8-2 of this title.
Any use allowed in zone R-1.
Fences as provided in section
9-8-1 of this title.
Mobile homes, permanently placed, used as a single-family dwelling:
All mobile homes in this zone shall be connected to sewer, water and
electricity and be set up on a permanent foundation with axles and tongues
removed.
Only one mobile home shall occupy one lot.
Setback, height and lot size restrictions for zone R-3 shall be the same as
those for zone R-1, except that mobile homes are restricted to one story in
height. (See definitions for "basement", "grade" and "story", as provided in
section
9-1-3 of this title.)
Minimum floor space shall be six hundred (600) square feet.
Mobile homes must be completely skirted.
Off street parking as provided in
chapter 9 of this title.
Preservation of historical sites as provided in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Retaining walls in accordance with the UBC (uniform building code).
Signs as provided in
chapter 10 of this title. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997; amd. Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
9-4C-2: STRUCTURE PER LOT:
There shall be only one main structure per lot. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
CHAPTER 5
COMMERCIAL ZONES USE REGULATIONS
ARTICLE A. C-1 ZONE
SECTION:
9-5A-1: Uses Permitted
9-5A-2: Firewall
9-5A-3: Refuse Area
9-5A-4: Loading, Unloading Space
9-5A-5: Setback, Height Restrictions
9-5A-1: USES PERMITTED:
In zone C-1, a building or premises shall be used only for the following
purposes:
Accessory buildings as provided in section
9-8-2 of this title.
Any use allowed in zone R-1.
Architecture as required in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended.
Banks and financial offices.
Fences as provided in section
 9-8-1 of this title.
Hospitals, clinics.
Municipal, state and federal government offices.
Off street parking as provided in
chapter 9 of this title.
Preservation of historical sites as required in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Professional offices, i.e., doctors, dentists, lawyers, accountants, etc.
Retaining walls in accordance with the UBC (uniform building code).
Signs as provided in
chapter 10 of this title. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-5A-2: FIREWALL:
A firewall is required where two (2) businesses or commercial enterprises share
a common wall. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-5A-3: REFUSE AREA:
An area for refuse containers shall be provided on the property. (Ord. 277, 10-
29-1997)
9-5A-4: LOADING, UNLOADING SPACE:
Any commercial establishment shall provide a minimum of one off street loading
or unloading space. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-5A-5: SETBACK, HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
Setback requirements as specified below are to be considered the minimum
measurement from the lot line to the physical building and any projections
thereof, including any roof overhang that exceeds three feet (3'). Landings
forty four inches (44") long having a width not more than the width of the door
served with stairs that same width shall not be considered a projection. (Ord.
277, 10-29-1997)
   A.   All buildings or premises that front on Burro Avenue from Glorietta
Avenue to Mescalero Avenue/Swallow Place may be built to the front and side lot
lines if a covered sidewalk is included as specified in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended and in the event such a
covered sidewalk is not included then a minimum front yard setback of fifteen
feet (15') is required on all premises and no side yard setback is required on
all premises except that a minimum side yard setback of eight feet (8') is
required on the street side of a corner lot. Rear yard setbacks to all of these
buildings or premises, with or without a covered sidewalk, are as specified in
subsections B3, B4 and B5 of this section. (Ord. 310, 10-8-2002)
   B.   For all buildings or premises that do not front on Burro Avenue from
Glorietta Avenue to Mescalero Avenue/Swallow Place:
      1.   A minimum front yard setback of fifteen feet (15') is required.
      2.   A minimum side yard setback of five feet (5') is required; a minimum
side yard setback of eight feet (8') is required on the street side of a corner
lot. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
      3.   A rear yard setback is not required if there is an alley along the
rear lot line, provided the required loading and unloading area and space for
refuse containers are located in a satisfactory manner elsewhere on the site
and there is no opening from the building into the alley. (Ord. 310, 10-8-2002)
      4.   A minimum rear yard setback of ten feet (10') is required if there
is an opening at the rear of the building.
      5.   A minimum rear yard setback of ten feet (10') is required if there
is no alley along the rear lot line.
   C.   No part of any building or structure shall exceed thirty feet (30') in
height above grade. (See definition for "grade" provided in section
9-1-3 of this title.) (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
ARTICLE B. C-2 ZONE
SECTION:
9-5B-1: Uses Permitted
9-5B-2: Firewall
9-5B-3: Refuse Area
9-5B-4: Loading, Unloading Space
9-5B-5: Setback, Height Restrictions
9-5B-1: USES PERMITTED:
In zone C-2, a building or premises shall be used only for the following
purposes:
Accessory buildings as provided in section
9-8-2 of this title.
Any use allowed in zone C-1.
Architecture as required in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended.
Fences as provided in section
9-8-1 of this title.
Off street parking as provided in
chapter 9 of this title.
Preservation of historical sites as required in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Retail and wholesale stores, i.e., any legal or licensed establishment engaged
in retail and wholesale sales and/or services, including laundromats and
storage units with the exception of those uses specified in zones C-3 through
M-1.
Retaining walls in accordance with the UBC (uniform building code).
Signs as provided in
chapter 10 of this title. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-5B-2: FIREWALL:
A firewall is required where two (2) businesses or commercial enterprises share
a common wall. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-5B-3: REFUSE AREA:
An area for refuse containers shall be provided on the property. (Ord. 277, 10-
29-1997)
9-5B-4: LOADING, UNLOADING SPACE:
Any commercial establishment shall provide a minimum of one off street loading
or unloading space. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-5B-5: SETBACK, HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
Setback requirements as specified below are to be considered the minimum
measurement from the lot line to the physical building and any projections
thereof, including any roof overhang that exceeds three feet (3'). Landings
forty four inches (44") long having a width not more than the width of the door
served with stairs that same width shall not be considered a projection. (Ord.
277, 10-29-1997)
   A.   All buildings or premises that front on Burro Avenue from Glorietta
Avenue to Mescalero Avenue/Swallow Place may be built to the front and side lot
lines if a covered sidewalk is included as specified in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended and in the event such a
covered sidewalk is not included then a minimum front yard setback of fifteen
feet (15') is required on all premises and no side yard setback is required on
all premises except that a minimum side yard setback of eight feet (8') is
required on the street side of a corner lot. Rear yard setbacks to all of these
buildings or premises, with or without a covered sidewalk, are as specified in
subsections B3, B4 and B5 of this section. (Ord. 310, 10-8-2002)
   B.   For all buildings or premises that do not front on Burro Avenue from
Glorietta Avenue to Mescalero Avenue/Swallow Place:
      1.   A minimum front yard setback of fifteen feet (15') is required.
      2.   A minimum side yard setback of five feet (5') is required; a minimum
side yard setback of eight feet (8') is required on the street side of a corner
lot. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
      3.   A rear yard setback is not required if there is an alley along the
rear lot line, provided the required loading and unloading area and space for
refuse containers are located in a satisfactory manner elsewhere on the site
and there is no opening from the building into the alley. (Ord. 310, 10-8-2002)
      4.   A minimum rear yard setback of ten feet (10') is required if there
if there is an opening at the rear of the building.
      5.   A minimum rear yard setback of ten feet (10') is required if there
is no alley along the rear lot line.
   C.   No part of any building or structure shall exceed thirty feet (30') in
height above grade. (See definition for "grade" as provided in section
9-1-3 of this title.) (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)

8-2002)
9-5I-4: LOADING, UNLOADING SPACE:
Any commercial establishment shall provide a minimum of one off street loading
or unloading space. (Ord. 307, 1-8-2002)
9-5I-5: SETBACK, HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
Setback requirements as specified below are to be considered the minimum
measurement from the lot line to the physical building and any projection
thereof, including any roof overhang that exceeds three feet (3'). Landings
forty four inches (44") long having a width not more than the width of the door
served with stairs that same width shall not be considered a projection. (Ord.
307, 1-8-2002)
   A.   All buildings or premises that front on Burro Avenue from Glorietta
Avenue to Mescalero Avenue/Swallow Place may be built to the front and side lot
lines if a covered sidewalk is included as specified in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended and in the event such a
covered sidewalk is not included then a minimum front yard setback of fifteen
feet (15') is required on all premises and no side yard setback is required on
all premises except that a minimum side yard setback of eight feet (8') is
required on the street side of a corner lot. Rear yard setbacks to all of these
buildings or premises, with or without a covered sidewalk, are as specified in
subsections B3, B4 and B5 of this section. (Ord. 310, 10-8-2002)
   B.   For all buildings or premises that do not front on Burro Avenue from
Glorietta Avenue to Mescalero Avenue/Swallow Place:
      1.   A minimum front yard setback of fifteen feet (15') is required.
      2.   A minimum side yard setback of five feet (5') is required; a minimum
side yard setback of eight feet (8') is required on the street side of a corner
lot. (Ord. 307, 1-8-2002)
      3.   A rear yard setback is not required if there is an alley along the
rear lot line, provided the required loading and unloading area and space for
refuse containers are located in a satisfactory manner elsewhere on the side
and there is no opening from the building into the alley. (Ord. 310, 10-8-2002)
      4.   A minimum rear yard setback of ten feet (10') is required if there
is an opening at the rear of the building.
      5.   A minimum rear yard setback of ten feet (10') is required if there
is no alley along the rear lot line.
   C.   No part of any building or structure shall exceed thirty feet (30') in
height above grade. (See definition for "grade" as provided in section
9-1-3 of this title.) (Ord. 307, 1-8-2002)

ARTICLE B. T-2 ZONE
SECTION:
9-6B-1: Permitted Uses
9-6B-2: Refuse Area
9-6B-3: Setbacks
9-6B-4: Height Restrictions

9-6B-1: PERMITTED USES:
In zone T-2, the property shall be used only for a recreational vehicle park
suitable for temporary location of mobile units. Zone T-2 may include the
following:
Accessory buildings as provided in section
9-8-2 of this title except that one service building of no more than six
hundred (600) square feet of gross floor area may be constructed even though no
main building is located on the premises; such service building must comply
with subsections
9-8-2A1 and A3 of this title and shall be used only to accommodate sanitary
conveniences, storage facilities, laundry and utility rooms.
Architecture as required in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended.
Fences as provided in section
9-8-1 of this title. Note: There shall be a solid fence not less than four feet
(4') nor more than six feet (6') in height on any side of the park that abuts
property under other ownership, excepting public rights of way, and which shall
comply with the requirements for fences in section
9-8-1 of this title.
Motor homes.
Off street parking for RV spaces shall be considered included in the individual
RV spaces.
Office unit, one, serving the administrative function of the park which shall
comply with zone R-1 requirements and may include the residence of the manager
of the park.
Pickup campers.
Preservation of historical sites as required in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Recreational vehicles (RVs).
Retaining walls in accordance with the IBC (international building code).
Signs; one sign not to exceed eight (8) square feet in area which shall comply
with the requirements for signs in
chapter 10 of this title.
Tents.
Trailers, including fifth wheels, pop-up campers. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6B-2: REFUSE AREA:
An area for refuse containers shall be provided on the property, except that a
recreational vehicle park with fewer than six (6) spaces shall be exempt from
this requirement. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6B-3: SETBACKS:
There shall be a minimum setback of ten feet (10') from a lot line to any RV
space or park building, except that the setback for any residence shall comply
with R-1 restrictions. The owner shall ensure that no RV, tent, trailer, pickup
camper or other occupant of the park encroaches on the area within the setback.
(Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6B-4: HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   No part of any building or structure shall exceed one story or twenty
feet (20') above grade except for the office unit/residence of the manager as
provided in section
9-6B-1 of this article. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6B-5: ENTRANCES, EXITS UNOBSTRUCTED:
Entrances and/or exits from the recreational vehicle park shall be visually
unobstructed. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6B-6: VILLAGE PERMIT REQUIRED:
The owner of the proposed RV park shall submit, in addition to the requirements
of section
9-2-3 of this title, a plan showing RV spaces, fences and utilities (including
dump stations). (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6B-7: ENVIRONMENTAL COMPLIANCE:
Each recreational vehicle park shall comply with all rules and regulations of
the state of New Mexico environmental division. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)

SECTION:

Accessory buildings as provided in section
9-8-2 of this title.
Architecture as required in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended.
Fences as provided in section
9-8-1 of this title.
Mobile homes.
Off street parking: each mobile home lot shall have a minimum of two (2)
parking spaces.
Office unit, one, serving the administrative function of the park which shall
comply with zone R-1 requirements and may include the residence of the manager
of the mobile home park.
Preservation of historical sites as required in ordinance to be adopted or as
may be amended.
Retaining walls in accordance with the IBC (international building code).
Signs; one sign not to exceed eight (8) square feet in area which shall comply
with the requirements for signs as provided in
chapter 10 of this title. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6C-2: REFUSE AREA:
An area for refuse containers shall be provided on the property. (Ord. 277, 10-
29-1997)
9-6C-3: LOADING, UNLOADING SPACE:
Any commercial establishment shall provide a minimum of one off street loading
or unloading space. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-6C-4: DENSITY:
A mobile home park may have no more than one mobile home lot per each three
thousand seven hundred fifty (3,750) square feet of total park property,
excluding land used for purposes other than the mobile home lots. (Ord. 333, 5-
10-2005)
9-6C-5: SETBACK, HEIGHT RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   There shall be a minimum setback of ten feet (10') from any park lot
line to any mobile home lot or park building, except that the setback from any
residence shall comply with R-1 restrictions.
   B.   Setback requirements for mobile home lots as specified below are to be
considered the minimum measurement from the mobile home lot line to the
physical building and any projection thereof, including any roof overhang that
exceeds three feet (3'). Landings forty four inches (44") long having a width
not more than the width of the door served with stairs that same width shall
not be considered a projection.
      1.   A minimum front yard setback of not less than twenty five feet
(25').
      2.   A minimum side yard setback of not less than seven and one-half feet
(71/2'), except that no part of any mobile unit shall be less than fifteen feet
(15') from the park property line.
      3.   A minimum rear yard setback of twenty five feet (25').
      4.   No part of any building or structure shall exceed one story or
fifteen feet (15') above grade except for the office unit/residence of the
manager as provided in section
9-6C-1 of this article. (See definitions for "basement", "grade" and "story" as
provided in section
9-1-3 of this title.) (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6C-6: PERMIT REQUIRED:
In addition to the requirements of section
9-2-3 of this title, a plan showing mobile home lots, fences and utilities
shall be submitted for the proposed mobile home parks. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6C-7: ENTRANCES, EXITS UNOBSTRUCTED:
Entrances and/or exits from the mobile home park shall be visually
unobstructed. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-6C-8: REGISTER MAINTAINED:
A register shall be kept and maintained consisting of the following
information:
   A.   Name and address of each occupant.
   B.   Make, model, year and license number of each mobile home and motor
vehicle.
   C.   State, county or territory issuing above licenses.
   D.   Date of arrival and departure of each mobile home. (Ord. 277, 10-29-
1997)
9-6C-9: FENCES:
There shall be a solid fence not less than four feet (4') nor more than six
feet (6') in height on any side of the park that abuts property under other
ownership, excepting public rights of way. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
9-6C-10: UTILITY CONNECTIONS:
Utility connections for mobile homes shall comply with all village and state
requirements for utility connections to buildings. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
CHAPTER 7
GREENBELT ZONES USE REGULATIONS
SECTION:
9-7-1: G-1 Zone
9-7-2: G-2 Zone
9-7-1: G-1 ZONE:
   A.   The G-1 zone shall consist of open space. No structures or commercial
signs shall be allowed, except that communication sites with structure and
necessary accessory buildings may be allowed by the governing body on property
owned by the village of Cloudcroft. (Ord. 340, 2-13-2007)
   B.   There shall be no overnight parking or camping allowed. (Ord. 277A, 8-
10-1999)
9-7-2: G-2 ZONE:
   A.   Uses Permitted: Permissive uses shall be public parks, recreation areas
and permitted communication sites as provided in zone G-1. (Ord. 340, 2-13-
2007)
   B.   Setbacks: Any permanent structures shall comply with the setbacks of
zone R-1.
   C.   Refuse Area: An area for refuse collection shall be provided.
   D.   Signs: Concessionaire signs shall comply with section
9-10-5 of this title, commercial zone signs.
   E.   Parking: Parking as provided in
chapter 9 of this title.
   F.   Overnight Parking, Camping: There shall be no overnight parking or
camping allowed without a special use permit. (Ord. 277A, 8-10-1999)
CHAPTER 8
REGULATIONS APPLICABLE TO ALL ZONES
SECTION:
9-8-1: Fences
9-8-2: Accessory Buildings
9-8-3: Public Health
9-8-4: Fire Stations
9-8-1: FENCES:
Fences shall be erected in compliance with the following requirements:
   A.   Height: Any fence located within the required front yard setback
established for each zone shall not be more than four feet (4') in height and
any other fence on the property shall not be more than six feet (6') in height,
except as follows:
      1.   Under automotive repair use in zone C-6, the vehicle storage area
shall be enclosed by a solid fence not less than six feet (6') nor more than
eight feet (8') in height. (See section
9-5F-1 of this title.) (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
      2.   Under automobile wrecking yard use in zone C-9, the storage area for
wrecked automobiles or other materials shall be enclosed by a solid fence not
less than six feet (6') nor more than eight feet (8') in height. (See section
9-5I-1 of this title.) (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997; amd. Ord. 307, 1-8-2002)
      3.   Under mobile home park use in zone M-1 and recreational vehicle park
use in zone T-2, there shall be a solid fence not less than four feet (4') nor
more than six feet (6') in height on all sides of the park. (See sections
 9-6C-1 and
9-6B-1, respectively, of this title.)
   B.   Visibility Intersecting Streets: To ensure proper visibility for
motorists, no solid fence may be located within fifteen feet (15') of the
intersecting street lot corner.
   C.   Parking Facility; Residential Zones: A parking facility adjacent to or
directly across the street from a residential zone shall be fenced with a solid
fence not less than four feet (4') nor more than six feet (6') in height. With
approval of the village, a hedge of suitable variety may be substituted for the
fence. (See subsection
9-9-4H of this title.)
   D.   Architecture: Architecture as required in ordinance 237 (see
title 8, chapter 2 of this code), or as may be amended for properties in zones
C-1 through M-1. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-8-2: ACCESSORY BUILDINGS:
   A.   Conditions: With the exception of subsection A4 of this section,
accessory buildings and uses in any zone shall be permitted only on the same
lot as the main structure in accordance with the following conditions:
      1.   Any such building shall comply with the setback requirements of the
zone in which it is located, except that:
         a.   Where the rear lot line does not abut an alley or other public
right of way, the rear setback shall be five feet (5').
         b.   Where the side lot line does not abut an alley or other public
right of way, the side setback shall be five feet (5').
         c.   Where the rear lot line abuts an alley, and there is no entrance
to the accessory building from the alley, the accessory building may be on the
alley line; similarly, where a side lot line abuts an alley, and there is no
entrance to the accessory building from the alley, the accessory building may
be on the alley line.
      2.   The gross floor area of an accessory building, or of the total of
all accessory buildings on the same lot, shall not exceed forty percent (40%)
of the area between the back of the main structure and the back lot line.
      3.   No part of any accessory building shall exceed one story or twenty
feet (20') in height above grade. (See "grade" as defined in section
 9-1-3 of this title.)
      4.   Where one entity owns two (2) or more contiguous lots, and a main
building exists on one of the lots, accessory buildings shall also be permitted
on the contiguous lots under the following conditions: There shall be no more
than one accessory building per lot; no accessory building shall exceed seven
hundred fifty (750) square feet in area; the use of the accessory building
shall be one permitted by the zoning of the lot on which it is constructed. In
zones R-1, R-2, R-3, T-1, T-2, and M-1 such accessory buildings shall be
maintained solely for the personal use of the occupants of the qualifying main
building. ("Personal use" does not include an office for a home occupation.) At
such time as an accessory building no longer conforms to the code because its
ownership is no longer the same as that of a contiguous lot with a qualifying
structure, the owner of the lot with the accessory building shall within one
year remove the structure, or convert it to a structure that meets the code
requirements for its zoning.
   B.   Construction And Use Of Accessory Buildings: Such accessory buildings
shall be built concurrently with or after the construction of the main building
and shall not be used as a dwelling or sleeping units.
   C.   Vehicles And Garages: No vehicle over twenty six thousand (26,000)
pounds' gross vehicle weight shall be housed in zones R-1, R-2, R-3, T-1, T-2,
M-1, G-1 or G-2. (Ord. 333, 5-10-2005)
   D.   Portable Buildings: A portable building no larger than two hundred
(200) square feet used as an accessory building shall be exempt from the
village permit requirements provided that such portable buildings shall be
installed according to the manufacturer's recommended standards, so long as
such standards comply with the state building code, and shall be subject to all
setbacks. The gross floor area of portable buildings shall be included in a
total area described in subsection A2 of this section. (Ord. 342, 6-13-2007)
9-8-3: PUBLIC HEALTH:
   A.   Construction sites and transportation of materials, as required in
section
4-1-8 of this code.
   B.   Nuisances, as prohibited in
title 4, chapter 2 of this code.
   C.   Chimneys and stovepipes, screening of, as regulated in subsection
4-2A-3B of this code, and fire hazards, noncombustible roofs and enclosed
eaves, as regulated in subsection
4-2A-3D of this code. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
9-8-4: FIRE STATIONS:
Fire stations shall be allowed in all zones. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
CHAPTER 9
OFF-STREET PARKING AND LOADING
SECTION:
9-9-1: Size
9-9-2: Parking Spaces Required
9-9-3: Parking Requirements For Uses Not Specified
9-9-4: General Provisions
9-9-1: SIZE:
Each parking space shall have:
   A.   Area: Minimum area of one hundred eighty (180) square feet.
   B.   Width: Minimum width of nine feet (9').
   C.   Ingress, Egress: Adequate room for ingress and egress.
   D.   One-Half Units, Measurements: When units or measurements determining
the number of required off-street parking and off-street loading spaces result
in a number of one-half (1/2) or greater, an additional space shall be
required.
   E.   Exceed Twenty; Size Reduction: When the determined number of required
parking spaces exceeds twenty (20), ten percent (10%) of the required spaces
may measure eight feet by sixteen feet (8' x 16') and be one hundred twenty
eight (128) square feet in area for compact vehicles.
   F.   Handicapped Parking: All commercial zones shall provide handicapped
parking in compliance with the current UBC.
   G.   Snow Removal: Provision for snow removal is the responsibility of the
owner. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
