9-9-3: PARKING REQUIREMENTS FOR USES NOT SPECIFIED:
The parking requirements for land uses which are not specified in this chapter
shall be determined by the Planning and Zoning Commission. Said determination
shall be based upon the requirements for the most comparable use specified
herein. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-9-4: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
   A.   Location: Off street parking facilities shall be located as hereinafter
specified:
      1.   For single-family and duplex dwellings, required parking shall be
located on the same lot as the building which it is required to serve.
      2.   For all other uses, required parking shall be located on the same
lot or on an abutting lot. Required parking shall not be located across a
public street or with an intervening property, except by conditional use permit
approved by the Planning and Zoning Commission. In the event a separately owned
lot is utilized, a lease shall be recorded with the Village Clerk- Treasurer.
      3.   In Commercial Zones C-1, C-2 and C-8, a variance from parking
requirements may only be obtained by paying to the Village a fee to be
determined by the Village Board of Trustees and based on the number of spaces
not provided. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
      4.   Burro Avenue retail parking from Glorietta Avenue to Mescalero
Avenue/Swallow Place and that fronting Lots 1 through 8 of Block 7 and Lots 1
through 3 of Block 1 of Skywater Subdivision on Village right-of-way, whether
acquired through plat dedication or conveyance, will be considered a single
parking lot (similar to a shopping mall) shared by all buildings and premises
that front these areas. Individual buildings and premises are not required to
provide additional off street parking. However, parking space requirements for
developments involving more than one lot as such may have been platted on the
effective date hereof, and fronting on the area of Burro Avenue from Glorietta
Avenue to Mescalero/Swallow Place will be the same as for developments not on
Burro Avenue. (Ord. 375, 6-13-2017)
   B.   Mixed Occupancies In Building: In the case of mixed uses in the
building or on a lot, the total requirements for off street parking facilities
shall be the sum of the requirements for the various uses computed separately.
Off street parking facilities for one use shall not be considered as providing
required parking facilities for any other use, except as hereinafter specified
for joint use.
   C.   Joint Use: The Planning and Zoning Commission may authorize joint use
of parking facilities when use of the facilities is primarily daytime for one
applicant and nighttime for the other, or weekdays for one applicant and
weekends for the other.
   D.   Submission Of Plans: The plans for any proposed commercial parking area
shall be submitted to the Planning and Zoning Commission at the time of the
application for a building permit for the building to which the parking area is
accessory. The plan shall clearly indicate the proposed development, including
location, size, shape, design, curb cuts, lighting, landscaping and other
features and appurtenances of the proposed parking lot.
   E.   Surface: All off street parking facilities shall be surfaced with base
course, concrete, asphaltic concrete, asphalt oil, or any other comparable
surfacing and shall be maintained in good condition, free of all weeds, trash
and other debris, and shall be properly drained, graded and cleared of snow.
   F.   Entrances And Exits: Entrances and/or exits shall be located at least
five feet (5') from any side lot line and at least twenty five feet (25') from
the side lot line on the street side of a corner lot.
   G.   Barriers: Wherever required to prevent vehicles using the parking
facility from encroaching upon the public streets, alleys or sidewalks, there
shall be provided a barrier not less than six inches (6") high.
   H.   Fences: Wherever a commercial parking facility abuts or is directly
across the street from any residence or residential zone, such parking facility
shall be isolated from such residence or residential zone by the construction
of a solid fence not less than four feet (4') nor more than six feet (6') in
height. With the approval of the Village, a hedge of suitable variety may be
substituted for such fence.
   I.   Lighting: Lighting shall comply with
title 8, chapter 3 of this Code.
   J.   Use Restrictions: The parking area shall only be used for passenger
vehicles and in no case shall be used for the commercial sale, repair work,
storage, dismantling or servicing of any vehicles, equipment, materials or
supplies. No vehicle over twenty thousand (20,000) pounds' gross vehicle weight
shall be housed in Zones R-1, R-2, R-3, T-1, T-2, M-1, G-1 or G-2.
   K.   Loading Berths: Any commercial establishment shall provide a minimum of
one off street loading or unloading space. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
CHAPTER 10
SIGNS
SECTION:
9-10-1: General Provisions
9-10-2: Exempt Signs Not Requiring Permit
9-10-3: Zones R-1 And R-3 Signs
9-10-4: Zone R-2 Signs
9-10-5: Commercial Zone Signs (C-1, C-2, C-3, C-4, C-5, C-6, C-7, C-8, C-9, C-
10, G-2, T-1, T-2, M-1)
9-10-6: Fees
9-10-1: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
   A.   Permit Required: Any sign which is not exempt shall require a village
sign permit.
   B.   Illumination: Exempt signs shall not be illuminated.
   C.   Flashing, Moving Lights: Signs shall not contain, include or be
illuminated by any flashing, intermittent or moving lights.
   D.   Resembling Official Signs: Signs shall not imitate or resemble any
official traffic sign, signal or device.
   E.   Commercial Signs On Trees: Commercial signs shall not be erected or
maintained upon trees.
   F.   Painting Signs On Rocks: Signs shall not be painted or drawn upon rocks
or other natural features. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
   G.   Upon Village Property: No sign except temporary unlit exempt signs as
described in subsection
9-10-2E of this chapter shall be erected on village property without a license
issued by the board of trustees. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
   H.   Attachment To Utility Poles: No signs shall be attached to utility
poles.
   I.   Obscuring Or Obstructing Traffic: Signs may not be located in such a
manner as to obscure or otherwise interfere with the effectiveness of an
official traffic sign, signal or device; or to obstruct, interfere with or
compromise the safety of vehicular or pedestrian traffic. (Ord. 277, 10-29-
1997)
   J.   Architecture: With the exception of temporary unlit exempt signs
described in subsections
9-10-2A, C, D, E, F and H of this chapter, all signs in zones C-1 through G-
2 shall comply with
title 8, chapter 2 of this code. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
   K.   Lighting: All signs shall comply with
title 8, chapter 3 of this code.
   L.   Location Within Lot Line: All components of a sign shall be located
within the lot lines of the lot on which it is erected. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-10-2: EXEMPT SIGNS NOT REQUIRING PERMIT:
   A.   Real Estate Signs: Real estate signs not exceeding four (4) square feet
in area and four feet (4') in height which advertise the sale, rental or lease
of the premises upon which they are located. Such signs shall be removed within
seven (7) days of the sale, closing, rental or leasing of said property.
   B.   Residential Name And Street Address Signs: One residential name and
street address sign so long as said sign is no more than two (2) square feet in
area and is attached to a structure. Such sign shall not project more than one
inch (1") beyond the face of the building. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
   C.   Temporary Unlit Banners:
      1.   Banner like signs, including, but not limited to, pennants, pennant
flap, streamers and fliers advertising a business or other for profit entity,
if approved in writing by the village administrator, may be displayed for not
more than fourteen (14) days in a twelve (12) month period.
      2.   Application shall be made on forms provided by the village and
submitted to the village administrator who shall refer such application to the
planning and zoning commission for comment. Such application shall include a
drawing of the sign reflecting color, size, and appearance, as well as the
number and proposed location.
      3.   Such banner like signs shall conform as provided in section
9-10-5 of this chapter and must utilize a western/railroad motif as provided in
section
8-2-6 of this code.
      4.   The village administrator after consideration of the comments by the
planning and zoning commission may issue written approval with such conditions
as determined to comply with the intent of this exemption with a copy to be
kept by the village clerk for at least twenty four (24) months. (Ord. 349, 5-
12-2009)
   D.   Temporary Political Signs: Temporary unlit political signs shall be
permitted up to a total area of six (6) square feet for each premises. Such
signs may be erected no earlier than thirty (30) days prior to any primary,
general or special election. They shall be removed within three (3) days after
the election to which the sign pertains. The candidate portrayed on the sign or
for whom the sign advertises shall bear the responsibility for removal. These
signs may only be placed on private property and shall not be attached to
utility poles.
   E.   Advertising For Community Or Civic Events: Temporary unlit signs
advertising community or civic events, and public entertainments presented by,
or for the benefit of, nonprofit entities as defined by section 501C3 of the
internal revenue code: such signs, if approved in writing by the village
administrator, may be erected no earlier than fourteen (14) days prior to the
event and shall be removed within three (3) days after the event. Copies of
such approval shall be filed with the village clerk/treasurer. The
administrator shall regulate the size, number and location of such signs. (Ord.
322, 10-14-2003)
   F.   Construction Signs: One construction sign on the construction site
which does not exceed ten (10) square feet in area. Such signs shall be removed
upon completion of the project.
   G.   Memorial Signs Or Tablets: One memorial sign or tablet not exceeding
three (3) square feet in area and permanently attached to the building or
structure.
   H.   Directional And Informational Signs: Directional and informational
signs displaying such legends as "self-service", "parking", "open", "closed",
"exit", "entrance", "lounge", "coffee shop", "office", "men's and women's
restrooms", "inflammable", including arrows, menus, etc., shall be allowed.
Each such sign shall not exceed two (2) square feet. It shall not be
permissible for the name of the business to appear on directional signs. (Ord.
277, 10-29-1997)
   I.   G-2 Public Parks And Recreation Signs: G-2 public parks and recreation
signs erected by the village, unlit and not exceeding sixteen (16) square feet
in area. (Ord. 277A, 8-10-1999)
9-10-3: ZONES R-1 AND R-3 SIGNS:
Only the following exempt unlit signs shall be allowed in zones R-1 and R-3:
   A.   Real Estate Signs: Real estate signs not exceeding four (4) square feet
in area and four feet (4') in height which advertise the sale, rental or lease
of the premises upon which they are located. Such signs shall be removed within
seven (7) days of the sale, closing, rental or leasing of said property.
   B.   Residential Name And Street Address Signs: One residential name and
street address sign so long as said sign is no more than two (2) square feet in
area and is attached to a structure. Such sign shall not project more than one
inch (1") beyond the face of the building.
   C.   Temporary Political Signs: Temporary political signs shall be permitted
up to a total area of six (6) square feet for each premises. Such signs may be
erected no earlier than thirty (30) days prior to any primary, general or
special election. They shall be removed within three (3) days after the
election to which the sign pertains. The candidate portrayed on the sign or for
whom the sign advertises shall bear the responsibility for removal. These signs
may only be placed on private property and shall not be attached to utility
poles.
   D.   Construction Signs: One construction sign on the construction site
which does not exceed ten (10) square feet in area. Such signs shall be removed
upon completion of the project.
   E.   Memorial Signs Or Tablets: One memorial sign or tablet not exceeding
three (3) square feet in area and permanently attached to the building or
structure. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-10-4: ZONE R-2 SIGNS:
   A.   Allowable Signs: Only the following exempt unlit signs shall be allowed
in zone R-2:
      1.   Real Estate Signs: Real estate signs not exceeding four (4) square
feet in area and four feet (4') in height which advertise the sale, rental or
lease of the premises upon which they are located. Such signs shall be removed
within seven (7) days of the sale, closing, rental or leasing of said property.
      2.   Residential Name And Street Address Signs: One residential name and
street address sign so long as said sign is no more than two (2) square feet in
area and is attached to a structure. Such sign shall not project more than one
inch (1") beyond the face of the building.
      3.   Temporary Political Signs: Temporary political signs shall be
permitted up to a total area of six (6) square feet for each premises. Such
signs may be erected no earlier than thirty (30) days prior to any primary,
general or special election. They shall be removed within three (3) days after
the election to which the sign pertains. The candidate portrayed on the sign or
for whom the sign advertises shall bear the responsibility for removal. These
signs may only be placed on private property and shall not be attached to
utility poles.
      4.   Construction Signs: One construction sign on the construction site
which does not exceed ten (10) square feet in area. Such sign shall be removed
upon completion of the project.
      5.   Memorial Signs Or Tablets: One memorial sign or tablet not exceeding
three (3) square feet in area and permanently attached to the building or
structure.
   B.   Business Sign; Nameplate: One business sign or nameplate requiring a
village sign permit and not exceeding eight (8) square feet in area shall be
permitted listing the name of the structure. This sign may be either attached
to a structure or freestanding. The bottom of a freestanding sign shall be no
more than one foot (1') above the ground.
   C.   Obscuring Or Obstructing Traffic: Signs may not be located in such a
manner as to obscure or otherwise interfere with the effectiveness of an
official traffic sign, signal or device, or to obstruct or interfere with or
compromise the safety of vehicular or pedestrian traffic.
   D.   Illumination: Illuminated signs shall be lighted in such a way that the
light source cannot be seen from the street or adjoining property and shall
comply with
title 8, chapter 3 of this code.
   E.   Location Within Lot Lines: All components of a sign shall be located
within the lot lines of the lot on which it is erected. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-10-5: COMMERCIAL ZONE SIGNS (C-1, C-2, C-3, C-4, C-5, C-6, C-7, C-8, C-9, C-
10, G-2, T-1, T-2, M-1):
   A.   Signs Attached To Structures:
      1.   The total signage on any single face of a structure shall not exceed
twenty percent (20%) of the area of that face.
      2.   No roof signs shall be allowed.
      3.   Illuminated signs shall be lighted in such a way that the light
source cannot be seen from the street or adjoining property and shall comply
with
title 8, chapter 3 of this code.
      4.   All signs shall comply with
title 8, chapter 2 of this code.
   B.   Freestanding Signs: Signs not attached to the face of a structure shall
be considered freestanding and shall comply with the following:
      1.   Only one freestanding sign shall be allowed on each lot.
      2.   Gasoline price signs; service stations shall be permitted one double
faced, on site sign not to exceed twelve (12) square feet per face and five
feet (5') in height advertising the price of gasoline. Such signs may be
freestanding so long as all of the criteria for a freestanding sign are met.
Such signs shall not contain any advertisement other than brand name. The
height limitation referred to above shall not apply to those gas price signs
which are mounted on a freestanding sign. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
      3.   The maximum area for any one freestanding sign shall be thirty two
(32) square feet where the height will not exceed the width of the actual sign,
with a maximum height of six feet (6'), including border and trim, whether on a
post or base from the ground elevation to its highest point. (Ord. 365, 9-10-
2013)
      4.   The area shall be measured by the smallest square, rectangle,
triangle, circle or combination thereof which will encompass the entire sign.
      5.   Freestanding signs may be placed back to back, side to side, stacked
or in V-type construction with not more than two (2) displays to each facing.
Such sign structure or structures shall be considered one sign.
      6.   Signs may not be located in such a manner as to obscure or otherwise
interfere with the effectiveness of an official traffic sign, signal or device;
or to obstruct, interfere with or compromise the safety of vehicular or
pedestrian traffic.
      7.   All components of a sign shall be located within the lot lines of
the lot on which it is erected.
      8.   Illuminated signs shall comply with
title 8, chapter 3 of this code.
      9.   Commercial zone signs shall comply with
title 8, chapter 2 of this code. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
9-10-6: FEES:
The board of trustees may establish fees to be submitted with all applications
for signs submitted to the village in accordance with the building permit
provisions of this title. (Ord. 277, 10-29-1997)
CHAPTER 11
CONTINUING USES
SECTION:
9-11-1: Continuing Uses
9-11-1: CONTINUING USES:
The lawful use of any premises existing on the effective date of Ordinance 277
may be continued although the use does not conform with the provisions hereof.
However, if a nonconforming use has been changed to a more restricted use or a
conforming use, it shall not thereafter be returned to a less restricted use.
Additions or alterations may be added to such structures without a variance,
provided the original structure location on the ground is maintained and no
other setback requirement is violated. (Ord. 277A, 8-10-1999)
CHAPTER 12
VARIANCES
SECTION:
9-12-1: Procedure For Variance
9-12-1: PROCEDURE FOR VARIANCE:
When a variance from a zoning regulation is requested, notice of a public
hearing shall be both published and mailed by certified mail, return receipt
requested, to the owners of all lots within one hundred feet (100'), excluding
public right-of-way, of the property requesting the variance and the notice
shall state that written protests will be reviewed and considered if received
in the Village offices by twelve o'clock (12:00) noon of the working day prior
to the scheduled public hearing. The notice shall also state that any public
hearing for a variance shall be conducted before the commission and the Board
of Trustees as set forth in this Code. This notice shall be published and
mailed at least fifteen (15) days prior to the date of the hearing. If the
owners of twenty percent (20%) or more of the area of those lots protest in
writing by twelve o'clock (12:00) noon on the workday prior to the scheduled
hearing, the variance shall not become effective unless the variance is
approved by a majority vote of all the members of the Board of Trustees. (Ord.
378, 1-9-2018)
TITLE 10
SUBDIVISION REGULATIONS 1
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
10-1-1: Territorial Coverage
10-1-2: General Procedures
10-1-3: Compliance With State Law
10-1-4: Fees For Application
 
Notes
1 1. NMSA § 3-20-1 et seq.
10-1-1: TERRITORIAL COVERAGE:
These subdivision regulations shall apply to all subdivisions within the
subdivision and platting jurisdiction of the Village as provided by County and
State law. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
10-1-2: GENERAL PROCEDURES:
   A.   Compliance Required: It shall be unlawful for anyone to create a
subdivision within the territorial coverage of the Village unless by plat, plan
and contract in accordance with the laws of the State and this Title.
   B.   Steps: The subdivider will follow these steps (unless qualified and
granted permission to follow the alternate procedures listed in Section
10-3-4 of this Title):
      1.   Step 1: The subdivider shall provide preliminary data (Section
10-3-1 of this Title) and shall comply with the preliminary procedure (Section
10-3-2 of this Title);
      2.   Step 2: At its next meeting, the Planning and Zoning Commission will
review and examine the written, platted and oral information provided by the
subdivider and make a recommendation to the Board of Trustees. (Ord. 287, 3-9-
1999)
      3.   Step 3: The Board of Trustees will approve or disapprove the plan
and preliminary plat. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999; amd. 2000 Code)
      4.   Step 4: If approval is given, the final plat (Section
10-3-3 of this Title) shall be submitted within six (6) months to the Planning
and Zoning Commission for its final approval and recommendation to the Board of
Trustees.
      5.   Step 5: The Board of Trustees will approve or disapprove the final
plat and plan. (With the approval of the Planning and Zoning Commission, the
subdivider may elect to combine the preliminary and final procedures, Steps 1
and 4.)
      6.   Step 6: Once the final plat has been approved by the Board, the
subdivider shall enter into a contract with the Village (Section
10-4-1 of this Title).
      7.   Step 7: Once the contract has been agreed to and signed by the
subdivider and the Village, the subdivider shall file and record the final plat
with the County Clerk. No construction, including excavation or earth work,
shall take place until the final plat has been filed and recorded with the
County Clerk. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
10-1-3: COMPLIANCE WITH STATE LAW:
The procedures established by State law for approval of subdivisions shall be
followed in all cases by the subdivider and the Board of Trustees. (Ord. 287,
3-9-1999)
10-1-4: FEES FOR APPLICATION:
Prior to the submission of a final plat to the Board of Trustees, the
subdivider shall pay to the Village a subdivision application fee to be
determined by the Board of Trustees. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
CHAPTER 2
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
10-2-1: Definitions
10-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this Title, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this Section:
   AVAILABLE WASTEWATER TREATMENT CAPACITY: Current capacity of existing
wastewater treatment plant less the current average influent in gallons per day
as determined by averaging the measurements of daily influent over the month of
July for the previous two (2) years.
   CUL-DE-SAC: A street with only one outlet culminated by a turnaround.
   EASEMENT: A grant from the property owner for the use, for specific
purposes, of a strip of land by the general public, or a certain person or
persons, or a corporation.
   FULL PUMPING CAPACITY: Average the number of gallons that could be pumped
per day over the month of July for each July for the previous five (5) years
(all wells running at maximum sustainable flow for 24 hours per day and all
spring water continuously collected).
   IMMEDIATE FAMILY MEMBER: Husband, wife, father, stepfather, mother,
stepmother, brother, stepbrother, sister, stepsister, son, stepson, daughter,
stepdaughter, grandson, stepgrandson, granddaughter, stepgrandaughter, nephew
and niece, whether related by natural birth or adoption.
   PERFORMANCE BOND: A surety bond made out to the Village of Cloudcroft in an
amount equal to the estimated full cost of the improvements; the cost being
estimated by a New Mexico licensed engineer retained by the subdivider and
under direction and control of the Village, with full approval of the Village,
and said surety bond being legally sufficient to secure to the Village of
Cloudcroft that the said improvements will be constructed accordance with
regulations as stated in the contract.
   PLAT OR REPLAT: A map, chart, survey or plan certified by a licensed
professional surveyor which contains a description of subdivided land with ties
to permanent survey monuments.
   SUBDIVIDER: Any person who creates or who has created a subdivision
individually or as part of a common promotional plan or any person engaged in
the sale, lease or other conveyance of subdivided land. However, "subdivider"
does not include licensed real estate brokers acting on another's account.
   SUBDIVISION: The division of a surface area of land, including land within a
previously approved subdivision, into two (2) or more parcels by platting or by
metes and bounds for the purpose of sale, lease or other conveyance or for
building development. However, "subdivision" does not include:
   A.   Division of land created by court order where the order creates no more
that one parcel per party;
   B.   Division of land resulting only in the alteration of parcel boundaries
where parcels are altered for the purpose of increasing or reducing the size of
contiguous parcels and where the number of parcels is not increased;
   C.   Division of land to create a parcel that is sold or donated as a gift
to an immediate family member; however, this exception shall be limited to
allow the seller or donor to sell or give no more than one parcel per tract of
land per immediate family member;
   D.   Division of land created to provide security for mortgages, liens or
deeds of trust; provided, that the division of land is not the result of a
seller-financed transaction. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999; amd. 2000 Code)
CHAPTER 3
PLAT PROCEDURES
SECTION:
10-3-1: Preliminary Data Requirements
10-3-2: Preliminary Procedure
10-3-3: Final Plat
10-3-4: Alternate Procedure
10-3-5: Water Rights
10-3-1: PRELIMINARY DATA REQUIREMENTS:
For subdivision located within the village limits, the supporting documentation
required before the preliminary plat is submitted shall provide sufficient
information for the village to determine:
   A.   Water: That sufficient potable water and sufficient pumping and/or
collection capacity at the water source will be available to meet the peak
daily demand flow rate (as measured by the peak daily discharge from the
potable water storage tanks) that has occurred during the previous three (3)
year period, plus the demand anticipated (at 600 gallons per lot per day) from
the subdivision when fully occupied.
   B.   Wastewater Plant Capacity: That the capacity of the wastewater
treatment plant facilities will be sufficient to meet peak daily water
treatment demands (as determined by the peak daily influent that has occurred
during the previous 3 year period), plus the demand anticipated (at 300 gallons
per day per lot) from the subdivision when fully occupied.
   C.   Single-Family Dwelling Assumption: All lots shall be assumed to be used
for single-family dwelling. If multi-family dwellings or other types of units
are to be constructed within the subdivision, then equivalency of single-family
units shall be used in the calculation of the eighty percent (80%) limit. If
other than single-family units, all capacity must be calculated pursuant to the
impact fee ordinance. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
10-3-2: PRELIMINARY PROCEDURE:
At his or her discretion and with the approval of the planning and zoning
commission, the subdivider may elect to combine the preliminary and final plat
procedures.
   A.   Information; Fee Required: Every owner of any tract of land situated
within the platting jurisdiction of the village who proposes to lay out any
subdivision or resubdivide any portion of an existing subdivision into any
parcels, streets, alleys, parks or other portions intended for public use
shall:
      1.   Pay the necessary filing fee to the village clerk/treasurer.
      2.   Submit five (5) copies of the preliminary plat at least five (5)
days prior to the next regular or special planning and zoning commission
meeting.
      3.   Submit a completed application form.
   B.   Scale: Plats shall be twenty four inches by thirty six inches (24" x
36") in size and show north point, scale and date. Minimum scale shall be one
inch equals one hundred feet (1" = 100').
   C.   Map Information: The preliminary plat map shall contain the following
information:
      1.   The dimensions and acreage of the land to be subdivided;
      2.   The location of present property lines; existing and abutting
streets or roads, utility easements and other easements; and other existing
features within and adjacent to the area to be subdivided;
      3.   Existing sewers, water mains, culverts and other underground
structures within the tract and immediately adjacent thereto; also, the
location and size of the nearest water main, sanitary sewer and other
utilities; plats for subdivisions in the extraterritorial jurisdiction shall
show location and capacity of water well or wells;
      4.   Provision for all other requirements of the subdivision regulations,
including, but not limited to, planning for terrain management, stormwater
management, water supply and delivery, solid liquid waste disposal, streets,
roads, emergency vehicle access, utility easements and alleys;
      5.   Proposed locations with widths of streets, alleys and easements, and
width, depth and acreage of lots, parks, parcels and blocks; all lots shall
meet minimum lot size requirements;
      6.   Legal description indicating the range, township and section within
which the subdivision is located and lot and block numbers;
      7.   The title under which the proposed subdivision is to be recorded,
the name of the subdivider platting the tract and the name of the licensed land
surveyor who prepared the plat;
      8.   The requested zoning classification and property use for the area
being subdivided;
      9.   Contours referred to in the United States Coast and Geodetic Survey
datum with intervals of two feet (2') or less in all areas excepting on slopes
averaging less than three percent (3%) where one foot (1') intervals shall be
required. For slopes over eight percent (8%), five foot (5') contour intervals
will be acceptable;
      10.   Any restrictive covenants governing the subdivision.
   D.   Recommendation By Commission: The Planning and Zoning Commission shall
make a recommendation to the Board of Trustees after examining and reviewing
the preliminary oral and written presentation by the subdivider to determine
that the Village subdivision regulations and requirements have been considered
and are to be followed in the final presentation of a subdivision plan by the
subdivider.
   E.   Board Decision: The Board of Trustees shall approve or disapprove the
plat. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
10-3-3: FINAL PLAT:
Within six (6) months of approval of the preliminary plat, the final plat shall
be submitted with two (2) Mylar copies and two (2) paper copies and shall be at
a scale of one hundred feet to one inch (1" = 100') or larger. Where necessary,
the plat may be on several sheets accompanied by an index sheet showing the
entire subdivision. It shall be submitted to the Planning and Zoning Commission
for approval prior to the submission to the Board of Trustees. The final plat
shall show the following:
   A.   All information required on a preliminary plat;
   B.   Tract boundary lines, right-of-way lines of streets and easements, and
property lines of residential lots and other sites; with accurate dimensions,
bearings or deflection angles and radii, arcs, and central angles of all
curves;
   C.   Name and right-of-way width of each street or other right of way, with
the street name continued if it is aligned with an existing street, with
streets and alleys abutting the subdivision drawn in dashed lines and named;
   D.   Location, dimensions, and purpose of any easements;
   E.   Number to identify each lot and block or tract;
   F.   Designation of any lots to be used for multiple dwellings;
   G.   Purpose for which sites, other than residential lots, are dedicated or
reserved;
   H.   Location and description of monuments;
   I.   Certification by a New Mexico registered land surveyor as to accuracy
of survey and plat;
   J.   Statement by owner dedicating streets, right of way and any sites for
public uses (together with dimensions of same);
   K.   Title, scale, north arrow and date;
   L.   Signed approval by authorized representatives of all utilities. (Ord.
287, 3-9-1999)
10-3-4: ALTERNATE PROCEDURE:
   A.   Conditions: When a subdivision consists of no more than two (2) parcels
of land or is a replat of previously filed subdivision which does not increase
the total number of lots by more than two (2) lots; and
      1.   All resulting lots meet minimum lot size requirements (see current
planning and zoning ordinance);
      2.   All Municipal liens on the subject property have been paid in full;
      3.   No provisions are required by the village for utilities, easements,
rights of way or drainage;
      4.   All owners of the subject property have signed the plat and
application;
      5.   None of the lots to be affected by the proposed subdivision have
been previously subdivided using the alternate subdivision procedure; and
      6.   Affected utility companies have signed releases;
then the planning and zoning commission may review the plat and make its
recommendation to the board of trustees. If the proposal is ineligible, the
commission will promptly notify the applicant that the full subdivision
procedure is required. The board of trustees will act on the recommendation of
the planning and zoning commission at its next regular or special meeting.
The planning and zoning commission may also review and make recommendations to
the board of trustees concerning replats which decrease the number of lots or
contiguous parcels in a previously filed subdivision; provided, that the items
provided in this subsection A are satisfied.
   B.   Submission Of Documents: The applicant is required to submit to the
village the following:
      1.   Completed application form, including waiver of public hearing;
      2.   Payment of the necessary filing fee to the village clerk/treasurer;
      3.   The original Mylar and two (2) copies of a final plat that meet all
the requirements of a final plat in section
10-3-3 of this chapter.
   C.   Waiver Of Rights Protected: By providing this alternate procedure, the
village does not waive its rights to require the applicant to satisfy any or
all of the village's usual requirements for subdivision approval. (Ord. 287, 3-
9-1999)
10-3-5: WATER RIGHTS:
   A.   Any subdivider of land not located within the original place of
Cloudcroft as shown on the original plat map filed of record, prior to the
approval of a final plat, shall be required to transfer to the village of
Cloudcroft sufficient water rights to serve all lots in the subdivision being
presented for approval.
   B.   "Sufficient water rights" shall be defined as the right to divert from
either surface or underground sources at least 0.45 acre-feet per annum per
lot.
   C.   Such water rights to be acceptable to the village must have been
accepted for filing as prima facie evidence of such right with the state
engineer of the state of New Mexico.
   D.   Such water rights shall be deemed to be acceptable when the state
engineer of the state of New Mexico has recognized or authorized a transfer of
such water rights the place of diversion, change of purpose of use to municipal
so that such water rights may be incorporated and used in the Cloudcroft
municipal water system by diversion from a surface source or a completed
functional well for diversion from an underground basin.
   E.   In lieu of a transfer of water rights, the subdivider may pay to the
village four thousand five hundred dollars ($4,500.00) for each lot. (Ord. 348,
4-14-2009)
CHAPTER 4
SUBDIVIDER REQUIREMENTS
SECTION:
10-4-1: Contract Required
10-4-2: Disclosure Statement
10-4-1: CONTRACT REQUIRED:
The subdivider shall be required to enter into a contract with the village,
agreeing to abide by and to comply with his layout and drawings, as finally
approved, and also all plans and specifications as approved, which contract
shall be reviewed annually and shall contain, among other provisions, the
following:
   A.   Repairs; Replacement: The subdivider shall be responsible for all
repairs to his construction work and the replacement of defective material or
workmanship on public property which may become apparent for a period of one
year after work has been completed and accepted by the village. (Ord. 287, 3-9-
1999)
   B.   Water, Sewer Lines: For subdivisions within the village limits, the
subdivider shall agree to supply and install all water lines and sewer lines of
approved weight and quality within the subdivision in accordance with village
standards, and also outside of the subdivision a sufficient distance to connect
with the village sewer and water system, and to furnish and install approved
weight and quality valves, fire hydrants, manholes, manhole rings and covers
with sewer stub outs and all appurtenances to the water and sewer systems. Fire
hydrants shall have a minimum of a four foot (4') radius clearance on all
sides; fire hydrants set into a bank shall have a wall or other device to
prevent rubble, dirt and runoff from collecting around them. Fire hydrants
shall be located so that the difference in grade between the hydrant and the
adjacent improved road is no greater than one foot (1'); the dirt level at the
hydrant shall be just below the mounting flange of the hydrant body.
Subdivisions outside the village limits but within the planning and platting
jurisdiction of the village shall provide an adequate supply of potable water
to each lot by a water system approved by the environment department (ED), but
not from water sources/aquifers within the village water rights area, without
village approval. Subdivisions outside the village limits but within the
planning and platting jurisdiction of the village shall connect to a public
sanitary sewer system if feasible. Where lots cannot be connected with a public
sewer system provisions must be made for sanitary sewerage treatment consisting
of a central treatment plant whose discharge meets all federal, state and local
standards and does not have the potential for contaminating the village ground
and surface water supply. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
   C.   Additional Water, Sewer Lines: Should the present sewer and water lines
and related appurtenances serving a subdivision within the village limits not
be adequate as determined by the village, the subdivider shall agree to bear
the cost of additional and/or replacement lines and appurtenances thereto in
order to carry the increased load made necessary by the subdivision.
   D.   Flood Protection: The subdivider shall agree to protect drainage
structures, to build bridges, culverts and other drainage facilities in the
area that may be necessary to protect the subdivision, the village and other
lands in the area from floods because of the development, and shall not change
the existing drainage patterns and quantities for any area outside of the
subdivision.
   E.   Damaged Facilities Repaired: Any damage caused by the subdivider to
existing water lines, sewer lines and/or any other infrastructure shall be
repaired at the subdivider's expense.
   F.   Licensed Engineer: The subdivider shall agree to retain and pay for the
services of a competent New Mexico licensed engineer to inspect all work as the
same progresses, make reports to the village, and certify in writing that all
work is in compliance with accepted engineering standards; the engineer shall
be under the direction and control of the village.
   G.   Performance Bond: The board of trustees shall require the subdivider to
post a performance bond in the full amount of one hundred percent (100%) of his
projected costs of development using a standard performance bond. (Ord. 287, 3-
9-1999)
   H.   Other Required Documents: A set of as built plans, and such other
certificates, affidavits, endorsements or deductions as may be required by the
board of trustees to ensure compliance with these regulations. (Ord. 322, 10-
14-2003)
10-4-2: DISCLOSURE STATEMENT:
The subdivider shall give to persons acquiring an interest in the subdivided
land a statement complying with the requirements of New Mexico Statutes
Annotated section 47-6-17. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
CHAPTER 5
IMPROVEMENTS; STANDARDS
SECTION:
10-5-1: Utilities Required
10-5-2: Streets
10-5-3: Public Sites And Open Spaces
10-5-1: UTILITIES REQUIRED:
All utilities, including water, sewer, electric transmission lines and street
improvements, shall be completed before any building permits shall be issued.
Utility design and construction shall be approved by the village and
appropriate utility providers. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
10-5-2: STREETS:
It is hereby required that all dedicated streets shall be a minimum of fifty
feet (50') in width, shall be cleared a minimum of twenty four feet (24') in
width, and shall be finished or paved a minimum of twenty two feet (22') in
width. In lieu of paving in a residential development, streets must have a
minimum depth of base course of four inches (4") after compaction with proper
drainage. Commercial subdivisions and commercial areas within subdivisions
shall be paved. Streets shall be constructed to New Mexico highway department
standards to include proper drainage. Street design and construction shall be
approved by the village. Streets which terminate in a cul-de-sac shall be no
longer than five hundred feet (500'); the terminus shall have a minimum
surfaced area radius of fifty feet (50'). Subdivider shall install street
signs, of a style selected by the village, at all intersections and such other
sites as may be determined by the village. (Ord. 322, 10-14-2003)
10-5-3: PUBLIC SITES AND OPEN SPACES:
   A.   Dedication For Park, Playground And Similar Spaces: Where a proposed
park, playground, school or other public use shown in a general community or
master plan is located in whole or in part in a proposed subdivision, the board
of trustees may require the dedication or reservation of such area, and in
cases of parks, the village shall develop the park within a reasonable time
after the subdivision has been completed. However, the subdivider shall not be
required to dedicate more than five percent (5%) of the total area of the
subdivision to the village for public use, exclusive of streets and alleys.
   B.   Other Areas: Where deemed essential by the board of trustees, upon
consideration of the particular type of development proposed in the
subdivision, and especially in large scale neighborhood unit developments, the
board of trustees may require the dedication or reservation of such other areas
or sites of a character, extent and location suitable to the needs created by
such development for schools, parks and other neighborhood purposes. However,
the subdivider shall not be required to dedicate more than five percent (5%) of
the total area of the subdivision to the village for public use, exclusive of
streets and alleys.
   C.   Pedestrian Easement: Any subdivision with a common boundary with a
national forest, or U.S. government or New Mexico state owned land, shall
provide a pedestrian easement every one-half (1/2) mile along the property line
shared by the subdivision and the public land. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
CHAPTER 6
VARIANCES
SECTION:
10-6-1: Authority
10-6-2: Conditions Imposed
10-6-1: AUTHORITY:
Where the Board of Trustees finds that extraordinary hardships may result from
strict compliance with these regulations, it may vary the regulations so that
substantial justice may be done and the public interest secured; provided, that
the variation will not have the effect of nullifying the intent and purpose of
this Title. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
10-6-2: CONDITIONS IMPOSED:
In granting variances and modifications, the Board of Trustees may require
conditions that will, in its judgment, secure substantially the objectives of
the standard or requirements so varied or modified. (Ord. 287, 3-9-1999)
CHAPTER 7
DEVELOPMENT FEE
SECTION:
10-7-1: General Provisions
10-7-2: Advisory Committee
10-7-3: Assumptions; Plan
10-7-4: Plan; Calculation Of Fee
10-7-5: Notice; Public Hearing
10-7-6: Accounting
10-7-1: GENERAL PROVISIONS:
   A.   State Law; Definitions: There is imposed in the Village a development
fee pursuant to laws 1993, chapter 122, and all definitions in such Act are
adopted herein and to which reference herein is made as State law.
   B.   Territorial Coverage: The development fee shall be assessed on any new
development of property within the Village limits.
   C.   Purpose: The development fee is imposed to pay the following specified
costs of constructing capital improvements or facility expansions as authorized
by State law.
   D.   Assessment And Collection: The development fee shall be assessed and
collected as provided by State law. (Ord. 288, 3-9-1999)
10-7-2: ADVISORY COMMITTEE:
Prior to adoption of a development fee, the Board of Trustees shall appoint a
Capital Improvements Advisory Committee, to be composed of not less than five
(5) members who shall be appointed by a majority vote of the Board of Trustees.
Not less than forty percent (40%) of the membership of the Advisory Committee
must be representative of the real estate, development or building industries.
No members shall be employees or officials of a municipality or county or other
governmental entity. The Advisory Committee serves in an advisory capacity and
shall:
   A.   Advise and assist the Board of Trustees in adopting land use
assumptions;
   B.   Review the capital improvements plan and file written comments;
   C.   Monitor and evaluate implementation of the capital improvements plan;
   D.   File annual reports with respect to the progress of the capital
improvements plan and report to the Board of Trustees any perceived inequities
in implementing the plan or imposing the development fee;
   E.   Advise the Board of Trustees of the need to update or revise the land
use assumptions, capital improvements plan and development fee. (Ord. 288, 3-9-
1999)
10-7-3: ASSUMPTIONS; PLAN:
   A.   Adoption Of Plan: Upon adoption of land use or system-wide assumptions,
the Village shall provide for a capital improvements plan to be developed by
qualified professionals using generally accepted engineering and planning
practices in accordance with State law.
   B.   Public Hearing: Upon completion of the capital improvements plan, the
Board of Trustees shall schedule and publish notice of a public hearing to
discuss the adoption of the capital improvements plan and imposition of the
development fee with notice as provided by State law.
   C.   Consolidation: The Board of Trustees may consolidate the land use
assumption and capital improvements as provided by State law.
   D.   Updating: The Board of Trustees shall update the land use assumptions
and capital improvements plan at least every five (5) years, and shall review
and evaluate its current land use assumptions and shall cause an update of the
capital improvements plan to be prepared and hold hearings in accordance with
State law. (Ord. 288, 3-9-1999)
10-7-4: PLAN; CALCULATION OF FEE:
A qualified professional shall prepare the capital improvements plan and
calculate the development fee in accordance with State law. The capital
improvements plan shall follow the infrastructure capital improvement planning
guidelines established by the Department of Finance and Administration and
shall address the following:
   A.   Description Of Existing Improvements: A description, as needed to
reasonably support the proposed development fee, which shall be prepared by a
qualified professional, of the existing capital improvements within the service
area and the costs to upgrade, update, improve, expand or replace the described
capital improvements to adequately meet existing needs and usage and strict
safety, efficiency, environmental or regulatory standards;
   B.   Analysis Of Capacity: An analysis, which shall be prepared by a
qualified professional, of the total capacity, the level of current usage and
commitments for usage of capacity of the existing capital improvements;
   C.   Description Of Expansions; Costs: A description, which shall be
prepared by a qualified professional, of all of the parts of the capital
improvements or facility expansions and their costs necessitated by and
attributable to new development in the service area based on the approved land
use assumptions;
   D.   Table Of Level, Quantity: A definitive table establishing the specific
level or quantity of use, consumption, generation or discharge of a service
unit for each category of capital improvements or facility expansions and an
equivalency or conversion table establishing the ratio of a service unit to
various types of land uses, including residential, commercial and industrial;
   E.   Number Of Projected Service Units: The total number of projected
service units necessitated by and attributable to new development within the
service area based on the approved land use assumption and calculated in
accordance with generally accepted engineering or planning criteria;
   F.   Projected Demand: The projected demand for capital improvements or
facility expansions required by new service units accepted over a reasonable
period of time, not to exceed ten (10) years. (Ord. 288, 3-9-1999)
10-7-5: NOTICE; PUBLIC HEARING:
To impose the development fee, the Village shall schedule and publish notice of
a public hearing, pursuant to the Village open meetings resolution to consider
land use assumptions, or system-wide land use assumptions, within the
designated service area that will be used to develop the capital improvements
plan, which public hearing shall be held and conducted in accordance with State
law. (Ord. 288, 3-9-1999)
10-7-6: ACCOUNTING:
All money collected through the adoption of a development fee shall be
maintained in separate interest-bearing accounts clearly identifying the payor
and the category of capital improvements or facility expansions within the
service area for which the fee was adopted with interest earned on development
fees to become part of the account on which it is earned and subject to all
restrictions placed on the use of development fees under State law. An annual
report describing the amount of any development fees collected, encumbered and
used during the preceding year by category of capital improvement and service
area identified as provided shall be a part of the annual audit process.
Disbursement from the separate accounts shall be made in accordance with State
law. (Ord. 288, 3-9-1999)
TITLE 11
FRANCHISES 1
CHAPTER 1
TELEPHONE FRANCHISE
SECTION:
11-1-1: Grant Of Authority
11-1-2: Company Liability
11-1-3: House Moving And Other Unusual Use
11-1-4: Tree Trimming
11-1-5: Consideration
11-1-6: Inspection Of Books
11-1-7: Payment In Lieu Of Other Taxes
11-1-8: Representation Of No Claims Under Prior Franchise
11-1-9: Alternative Dispute Resolution
11-1-10: Notices
11-1-11: Annexation
11-1-12: Nonwaiver Of Other Rights
11-1-13: Term Of Franchise
11-1-14: Effective Date
11-1-15: Severability Clause
11-1-16: Appendix A
 
Notes
1 1. NMSA § 3-42-1.
11-1-1: GRANT OF AUTHORITY:
There is hereby granted by the village of Cloudcroft, hereinafter called the
"village" to Tularosa Basin Telephone Company, its successors and assigns,
hereinafter called the "company", the nonexclusive right and privilege to
construct, erect, operate and maintain, in, upon, along, across, above, over
and under the streets, alleys, public ways and public places now in use or
dedicated, and all extensions thereof, and additions thereto, in said village,
poles, wires, cables, underground conduits, manholes and other
telecommunications facilities necessary or proper for the maintenance and
operation in said village of Cloudcroft of the company's telecommunications
business; provided, however, that no poles or other facilities shall be placed
where the same will interfere with any street, roadway or traffic control
facilities or with any existing utility facilities and shall be placed in such
a manner as to cause a minimum interference with the rights or reasonable
convenience of property owners who adjoin any of said streets, alleys or public
ways and places. Any and all changes made by the company for company reasons in
the location of the poles, wires, cables, underground conduits, manholes and
other telecommunications facilities shall not require the village to pay for
the change in any street, roadway or traffic control facility caused by the
change of the locations by the company. The cost thereof shall be paid by the
company. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-2: COMPANY LIABILITY:
The company shall, at all times during the life of this franchise, be subject
to all lawful exercise of the police power by the village and to such
regulations as the village may, by resolution or ordinance, hereafter provide.
It is expressly understood and agreed by and between the company and village
that the company shall save the village harmless from all loss sustained by the
village on account of any suit, judgment, execution, claim or demand
whatsoever, resulting from negligence on the part of the company in the
construction or maintenance of its telecommunications system in the village.
The village shall notify the company's representative in writing at P.O. Box
550, Tularosa, NM 88352, within ten (10) days after the service of process in a
suit against the village on account of any negligence as aforesaid on the part
of the company. Failure to promptly notify the company as required above shall
operate as release of the company's obligation to save the village harmless
regarding the claim or demand if such failure of notice results in substantial
harm to the company. The village will forward a copy of any notice of claim
made under the state tort claims act involving the company within a reasonable
period of time. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-3: HOUSE MOVING AND OTHER UNUSUAL USE:
Any person or corporation desiring to move a building or other structure along,
or to make any unusual use of, the streets, alleys and public ways of the
village which shall interfere with the poles, wires or facilities of the
company or the village, shall first give notice to the company or the village,
as the case may be, and a sum sufficient to cover the expense and damages
incident to the cutting, altering and moving of the wires or other facilities
of the company or the village, and before a permit is given by the village
therefor, the applicant shall present a receipt from the company showing the
payment. Thereupon the company, upon presentation of said permit, shall within
a reasonable time thereafter provide for and do such cutting, altering and
moving of said wires and facilities as may be necessary to allow such moving or
other unusual use of the streets, alleys and public ways of the village. (Ord.
371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-4: TREE TRIMMING:
The company shall have the authority, to the extent that the village has such
authority, to trim trees upon or overhanging streets, highways, alleys, bridges
or other public ways or places of the village in order to prevent the branches
of such trees from coming in contact with the wires, cables, conductors or
other facilities or equipment of the company; provided, however, that the
company shall obtain permission of any landowner should it be necessary to trim
any tree where the main trunk is located on private property. (Ord. 371, 3-15-
2016)
11-1-5: CONSIDERATION:
As a further consideration for this franchise, the company shall pay to the
village franchise payments in an amount equal to three percent (3%) of the
gross monthly recurring revenues, exclusive of all federal and state excise
taxes, from the services listed in section
11-1-16, "Appendix A", of this chapter, furnished to subscribers of the
company, not including uncollectible revenues related to those services within
the village of Cloudcroft. Payment shall be made in quarterly installments
within sixty (60) days after the end of each calendar quarter during the term
of this franchise. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-6: INSPECTION OF BOOKS:
The village shall have the right, at all reasonable times, to inspect the books
and records of the company pertaining to the company's gross monthly recurring
revenues from the services listed in section
11-1-16, "Appendix A", of this chapter received from the company's subscribers
located within the limits of the village. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-7: PAYMENT IN LIEU OF OTHER TAXES:
In consideration of the franchise payments hereinabove provided for, it is
expressly understood and agreed by the company and the village that these
payments shall be in lieu of any and all other franchise, license, occupation
or other forms of excise or revenue taxes based upon or measured by the
revenues, employees, payroll, property, facilities or equipment of the company,
excepting, however, general ad valorem property taxes, special assessments for
local improvements and sales or gross receipts taxes (all hereinafter referred
to as "excepted taxes"). The franchise payments shall continue only so long as
the company is not prohibited from making the payments by any lawful authority
having jurisdiction in the premises. Furthermore, if the village does levy,
charge or collect or attempt to levy, charge or collect any other franchise,
license, occupation or other form of excise or revenue taxes of the type above
specified in this paragraph (other than excepted taxes), the obligation to make
franchise payments hereunder shall be abated to the extent such other taxes are
levied, charged or collected by the village. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-8: REPRESENTATION OF NO CLAIMS UNDER PRIOR FRANCHISE:
The village and the company recognize the existence of and validity of
ordinances 338 and 338A, previously granting a franchise to Tularosa Basin
Telephone Company ("company"), and agree that the prior franchise has been
extended by mutual agreement in order to negotiate this agreement, it being the
intent and understanding that there are no claims by the village against
Tularosa Basin Telephone Company or the company and no claims by Tularosa Basin
Telephone Company or the company against the village with respect to the
locations, establishment, construction, maintenance or operation of the
company's lines and facilities within the village, or amounts due to the
village under the prior franchise. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-9: ALTERNATIVE DISPUTE RESOLUTION:
   A.   Any party considering the other to be in default of this agreement
shall give the other written notice of the default. The party receiving the
notice shall have thirty (30) days to remedy the default or within which to
commence actions to remedy the default, if the default cannot reasonably be
remedied within thirty (30) days. If the party alleged to be in default fails
to remedy the default within the prescribed period or to complete remedial
actions within a reasonable time, the other party may, upon sixty (60) days'
written notice, elect to cancel this agreement, subject to payment of any
accrued amounts due under section
11-1-5 of this chapter.
   B.   The parties desire to resolve disputes arising out of this chapter
without litigation. Accordingly, in the event of any dispute hereunder, the
parties agree to attempt to negotiate in good faith to resolve any dispute
arising under this chapter. The parties intend that these negotiations shall be
conducted by nonlawyer, business representatives.
   C.   Except for action seeking a temporary restraining order or injunction
related to the purposes of this chapter, or suit to compel compliance with this
dispute resolution process, the parties agree to use the following alternative
dispute resolution procedure and also agree not to sue any party to this
chapter with respect to any controversy or claim arising out of or relating to
this chapter or its breach prior to exhausting the procedures set out in this
section.
   D.   If the parties are unable to settle their dispute within sixty (60)
days of the initial request, either party may, on written notice to the other
party, initiate nonbinding mediation of the dispute before a single mediator.
The mediator shall be selected by agreement of the parties within thirty (30)
days after one of the parties has requested mediation. If a single mediator
cannot be agreed upon, each party shall select its own mediator and those
mediators shall select an independent mediator who will conduct the mediation
session(s). The mediator fees shall be borne equally by both parties. The
mediation shall be completed by recommendation of the mediation panel submitted
to both parties within thirty (30) days after selection of the entire mediation
panel.
Unless the parties agree otherwise, all matters, including the communications,
conduct and demeanor of the parties and their counsel during mediation, are
confidential and shall be inadmissible as settlement discussions in any
subsequent litigation. In the event mediation fails, the parties may resort to
means outside the scope of this section to resolve their dispute. (Ord. 371, 3-
15-2016)
11-1-10: NOTICES:
Written notice to the village shall be sent to Mayor, Village Of Cloudcroft at
P.O. Box 817, Cloudcroft, NM 88317. Written notice to the company shall be sent
to General Manager, Tularosa Basin Telephone Company, P.O. Box 550, Tularosa,
NM 88352. Hand delivery is acceptable. However, receipt shall be acknowledged.
(Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-11: ANNEXATION:
Upon any annexation of territory to the village, any gross monthly recurring
revenues from the services listed in section
11-1-16, "Appendix A", of this chapter received from subscribers located within
the annexed area listed shall be included in the base for computation of
payments due to the village. Such inclusion shall be effective thirty (30) days
after written notice to the company of such annexation is delivered by the
village to the company. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-12: NONWAIVER OF OTHER RIGHTS:
It is expressly understood and agreed by and between the village and the
company that neither the grant nor acceptance of this franchise shall
constitute a waiver, either upon the part of the company or the village, of any
rights or claims had or made by either with respect to the occupancy of the
streets, alleys and public places of the village, under the constitution and
laws of the state of New Mexico, nor shall anything herein in any way prejudice
or impair any rights or claims existing independently of this franchise of the
village or the company, or its predecessors or successors, with respect to the
construction, operation and maintenance, either before or after the life of
this franchise, of a telecommunications system in the village. (Ord. 371, 3-15-
2016)
11-1-13: TERM OF FRANCHISE:
The franchise and rights herein granted shall continue in force and effect for
a term of ten (10) years after the effective date of this franchise. (Ord. 371,
3-15-2016)
11-1-14: EFFECTIVE DATE:
This chapter shall become effective thirty (30) days after its enactment,
provided the company within those thirty (30) days, shall have filed with the
village clerk of the village of Cloudcroft an unconditional acceptance thereof
and acknowledge the obligation to pay for the publication of the ordinance.
Within ten (10) days after the filing of the acceptance, the village clerk
shall acknowledge in writing the receipt of the company's acceptance and
publish the ordinance. (Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
11-1-15: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, sentence, clause, word or phrase of this chapter is
for any reason held to be unconstitutional or otherwise invalid by any court of
competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity of the
remaining portions of this chapter. The board of trustees, the governing body
of the village of Cloudcroft, hereby declares that it would have passed this
chapter and each section, subsection, sentence, clause, word or phrase thereof
regardless of any one or more sections, subsections, sentences, clauses, words
or phrases being declared unconstitutional or otherwise invalid. (Ord. 371, 3-
15-2016)
11-1-16: APPENDIX A:
   APPENDIX A
- Business dial tone line
- Business local service increments
- Business flat usage and multiparty service
- Business measured usage services
- Flat usage trunks
- Low income telephone assistance program
- Measured rate trunk usage
- Message rate trunk usage
- Public access line (PAL) services
- Residence dial tone
- Residence flat usage and multiparty service
- Residence local service increments
(Ord. 371, 3-15-2016)
CHAPTER 2
CABLE TELEVISION FRANCHISE
SECTION:
11-2-1: Grant Of Authority
11-2-2: Company Liability
11-2-3: Housemoving And Other Unusual Use
11-2-4: Tree Trimming
11-2-5: Consideration
11-2-6: Inspection Of Books
11-2-7: Payment In Lieu Of Other Taxes
11-2-8: Representation Of No Claims Under Prior Franchise
11-2-9: Alternative Dispute Resolution
11-2-10: Notices
11-2-11: Annexation
11-2-12: Non-Waiver Of Other Rights
11-2-13: Term Of Franchise
11-2-14: Effective Date
11-2-15: Severability Clause
11-2-16: Appendix A
11-2-1: GRANT OF AUTHORITY:
There is hereby granted by the Village of Cloudcroft, hereinafter called the
"Village" to PVT NetWorks, Inc., its successors and assigns, hereinafter called
the "company", the non-exclusive right and privilege to construct, erect,
operate and maintain, in, upon, along, across, above, over and under the
streets, alleys, public ways and public places now in use or dedicated, and all
extensions thereof, and additions thereto, in said Village, poles, wires,
cables, underground conduits, manholes and other telecommunications facilities
necessary or proper for the maintenance and operation in said Village of
Cloudcroft of the company's telecommunications business supplying television
signals, voice, high speed data services and security systems; provided,
however, that no poles or other facilities shall be placed where the same will
interfere with any street, roadway or traffic control facilities or with any
existing utility facilities and shall be placed in such a manner as to cause a
minimum interference with the rights or reasonable convenience of property
owners who adjoin any of said streets, alleys or public ways and places. Any
and all changes made by the company for company reasons in the location of the
poles, wires, cables, underground conduits, manholes and other communications
facilities shall not require the Village to pay for the change in any street,
roadway or traffic control facility caused by the change of the locations by
the company. The cost thereof shall be paid by the company. (Ord. 376, 7-11-
2017)
11-2-2: COMPANY LIABILITY:
The company shall, at all times during the life of this franchise, be subject
to all lawful exercise of the police power by the Village and to such
regulations as the Village may, by resolution or ordinance, hereafter provide.
It is expressly understood and agreed by and between the company and Village
that the company shall save the Village harmless from all loss sustained by the
Village on account of any suit, judgment, execution, claim or demand
whatsoever, resulting from negligence on the part of the company in the
construction or maintenance of its telecommunications system in the Village.
The Village shall notify the company's representative in writing at 4011 West
Main St., Artesia, New Mexico 88210, within ten (10) days after the service of
process in a suit against the Village on account of any negligence as aforesaid
on the part of the company. Failure to promptly notify the company as required
above shall operate as release of the company's obligation to save the Village
harmless regarding the claim or demand if such failure of notice results in
substantial harm to the company. The Village will forward a copy of any notice
of claim made under the State Tort Claims Act involving the company within a
reasonable period of time. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-3: HOUSEMOVING AND OTHER UNUSUAL USE:
Any person or corporation desiring to move a building or other structure along,
or to make any unusual use of, the streets, alleys and public ways of the
Village which shall interfere with the poles, wires or facilities of the
company or the Village, shall first give notice to the company or the Village,
as the case may be, and a sum sufficient to cover the expense and damages
incident to the cutting, altering and moving of the wires or other facilities
of the company or the Village, and before a permit is given by the Village
therefor the applicant shall present a receipt from the company showing the
payment. Thereupon the company, upon presentation of said permit, shall within
a reasonable time thereafter provide for and do such cutting, altering and
moving of said wires and facilities as may be necessary to allow such moving or
other unusual use of the streets, alleys and public ways of the Village. (Ord.
376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-4: TREE TRIMMING:
The company shall have the authority, to the extent that the Village has such
authority, to trim trees upon or overhanging streets, highways, alleys, bridges
or other public ways or places of the Village in order to prevent the branches
of such trees from coming in contact with the wires, cables, conductors, or
other facilities or equipment of the company; provided, however, that the
company shall obtain permission of any landowner should it be necessary to trim
any tree where the main trunk is located on private property. (Ord. 376, 7-11-
2017)
11-2-5: CONSIDERATION:
As a further consideration for this franchise, the company shall pay to the
Village franchise payments in an amount equal to three percent (3%) of the
gross monthly recurring revenues, exclusive of all Federal and State Excise
Taxes, from the services listed in section
11-2-16, "Appendix A", of this chapter, furnished to subscribers of the
company, not including uncollectible revenues related to those services within
the Village of Cloudcroft. Payment shall be made in quarterly installments
within sixty (60) days after the end of each calendar quarter during the term
of this franchise. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-6: INSPECTION OF BOOKS:
The Village shall have the right, at all reasonable times, to inspect the books
and records of the company pertaining to the company's gross monthly recurring
revenues from the services listed in section
11-2-16, "Appendix A", of this chapter received from the company's subscribers
located within the limits of the Village. Considering that this does not
violate any CPNI rules. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-7: PAYMENT IN LIEU OF OTHER TAXES:
In consideration of the franchise payments herein above provided for, it is
expressly understood and agreed by the company and the Village that these
payments shall be in lieu of any and all other franchise, license, occupation,
or other forms of Excise or Revenue Taxes based upon or measured by the
revenues, employees, payroll, property, facilities or equipment of the company,
excepting, however, General Ad Valorem Property Taxes, special assessments for
local improvements and Sales or Gross Receipts Taxes (all hereinafter referred
to as "excepted taxes"). The franchise payments shall continue only so long as
the company is not prohibited from making the payments by any lawful authority
having jurisdiction in the premises. Furthermore, if the Village does levy,
charge or collect or attempt to levy, charge or collect any other franchise,
license, occupation or other form of Excise or Revenue Taxes of the type above
specified in this paragraph (other than excepted taxes), the obligation to make
franchise payments hereunder shall be abated to the extent such other taxes are
levied, charged or collected by the Village. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-8: REPRESENTATION OF NO CLAIMS UNDER PRIOR FRANCHISE:
The Village and the company recognize the existence of ordinance 32, which is
repealed by this chapter, previously granting a franchise to Cloudcroft TV
Company a predecessor in interest to the company, and agree that the prior
franchise has been recognized as effective by mutual agreement, it being the
intent and understanding that there are no claims by the Village against
Cloudcroft TV or the company and no claims by Cloudcroft TV or the company
against the Village with respect to the location, establishment, construction,
maintenance or operation of the company's lines and facilities within the
Village, or amounts due to the Village under the prior franchise. (Ord. 376, 7-
11-2017)
11-2-9: ALTERNATIVE DISPUTE RESOLUTION:
   A.   Any party considering the other to be in default of this agreement
shall give the other written notice of the default. The party receiving the
notice shall have thirty (30) days to remedy the default or within which to
commence actions to remedy the default, if the default cannot reasonably be
remedied within thirty (30) days. If the party alleged to be in default fails
to remedy the default within the prescribed period or to complete remedial
actions within a reasonable time, the other party may, upon sixty (60) days
written notice, elect to cancel this agreement, subject to payment of any
accrued amounts due under section
11-2-5 of this chapter.
   B.   The parties desire to resolve disputes arising out of this chapter
without litigation. Accordingly, in the event of any dispute hereunder, the
parties agree to attempt to negotiate in good faith to resolve any dispute
arising under this chapter. The parties intend that these negotiations shall be
conducted by non-lawyer, business representatives.
   C.   Except for action seeking a temporary restraining order or injunction
related to the purposes of this chapter, or suit to compel compliance with this
dispute resolution process, the parties agree to use the following alternative
dispute resolution procedure and also agree not to sue any party to this
chapter with respect to any controversy or claim arising out of or relating to
this chapter or its breach prior to exhausting the procedures set out in this
section.
   D.   If the parties are unable to settle their dispute within sixty (60)
days of the initial request, either party may, on written notice to the other
party, initiate non-binding mediation of the dispute before a single mediator.
The mediator shall be selected by agreement of the parties within thirty (30)
days after one of the parties has requested mediation. If a single mediator
cannot be agreed upon, each party shall select its own mediator and those
mediators shall select an independent mediator who will conduct the mediation
session(s). The mediator's fees shall be borne equally by both parties. The
mediation shall be completed by recommendation of the mediation panel submitted
to both parties within thirty (30) days after selection of the entire mediation
panel.
Unless the parties agree otherwise, all matters, including the communications,
conduct and demeanor of the parties and their counsel during mediation, are
confidential and shall be inadmissible as settlement discussions in any
subsequent litigation. In the event mediation fails, the parties may resort to
means outside the scope of this section to resolve their dispute. (Ord. 376, 7-
11-2017)
11-2-10: NOTICES:
Written notice to the Village shall be sent to: Mayor, Village of Cloudcroft at
PO Box 817, Cloudcroft, New Mexico 88317. Written notice to the company shall
be sent to: General Manager, PVT NetWorks, Inc, 4011 West Main Street, Artesia,
New Mexico 88210. Hand-delivery is acceptable. However, receipt shall be
acknowledged. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-11: ANNEXATION:
Upon any annexation of territory to the Village, any gross monthly recurring
revenues from the services listed in section
11-2-16, "Appendix A", of this chapter received from subscribers located within
the annexed area listed shall be included in the base for computation of
payments due to the Village. Such inclusion shall be effective thirty (30) days
after written notice to the company of such annexation is delivered by the
Village to the company. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-12: NON-WAIVER OF OTHER RIGHTS:
It is expressly understood and agreed by and between the Village and the
company that neither the grant nor acceptance of this franchise shall
constitute a waiver, either upon the part of the company or the Village, of any
rights or claims had or made by either with respect to the occupancy of the
streets, alleys, and public places of the Village, under the Constitution and
laws of the State of New Mexico, nor shall anything herein in any way prejudice
or impair any rights or claims existing independently of this franchise of the
Village or the company, or its predecessors or successors, with respect to the
construction, operation, and maintenance, either before or after the life of
this franchise, of a telecommunications system in the Village. (Ord. 376, 7-11-
2017)
11-2-13: TERM OF FRANCHISE:
The franchise and rights herein granted shall continue in force and effect for
a term of ten (10) years after the effective date of this franchise. (Ord. 376,
7-11-2017)
11-2-14: EFFECTIVE DATE:
This chapter shall become effective thirty (30) days after its enactment,
provided the company within those thirty (30) days, shall have filed with the
Village Clerk-Treasurer of the Village of Cloudcroft an unconditional
acceptance thereof and acknowledge the obligation to pay for the publication of
the ordinance. Within ten (10) days after the filing of the acceptance, the
Village Clerk-Treasurer shall acknowledge in writing the receipt of the
company's acceptance and publish the ordinance. (Ord. 376, 7-11-2017)
11-2-15: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
If any section, subsection, sentence, clause, word or phrase of this chapter is
for any reason held to be unconstitutional or otherwise invalid by any court of
competent jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity of the
remaining portions of the chapter. The Board of Trustees, the Governing Body of
the Village of Cloudcroft, hereby declares that it would have passed this
chapter and each section, asubsection, sentence, clause, word or phrase thereof
regardless of any one or more sections, subsections, sentences, clauses, words
or phrases being declared unconstitutional or otherwise invalid. (Ord. 376, 7-
11-2017)
11-2-16: APPENDIX A:
Communication activities including voice, data, video and security system and
to the extent applicable:
Business dial tone line
Business flat usage and multiparty service
Business local service increments
Business measured usage services
Flat usage trunks
